Divine Attributes
beginner
4 min
The Third State: Affirming Attributes Without Takyif or Tashbih
Describes the third state of affirming divine attributes without takyif or tashbih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the correct methodology for divine attributes according to al-Ash'ari is to affirm them without asking how or making any likeness, following the path of the Salaf.

Core Idea
Affirm attributes without modality or similitude — that is the way of the Salaf.

In this passage from al-Ibanah, Imam al-Ash'ari explains the third and final state regarding the divine attributes. He emphasizes that attributes like power, will, hearing, sight, speech, and the khabari attributes (face, hands, foot, shin) are to be affirmed without any attempt to specify modality (takyif) or to compare them to creation (tashbih). This approach mirrors the methodology of the Salaf, which al-Ash'ari adopted in his later work.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the list of attributes and the phrase 'إثبات ذلك كله من غير تكييف ولا تشبيه'.
The key phrase is 'without takyif or tashbih'.
2
Identify the attributes mentioned
The passage lists essential attributes (power, will, hearing, sight, speech) and khabari attributes (face, hands, foot, shin). Understand that these are all to be affirmed.
Khabari attributes are those that occur in revelation but may seem anthropomorphic.
3
Understand the third state
The 'third state' is affirming all these attributes without specifying modality (takyif) or making any likeness (tashbih). This is the middle path between negation and anthropomorphism.
The first two states are not mentioned here but traditionally are rejection or interpretation.
4
Connect to the Salaf and al-Ash'ari's methodology
Al-Ash'ari states that this method follows the path of the Salaf and is his approach in al-Ibanah. Reflect on why this is important for avoiding both extremes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقدرة ، والإرادة ، والسمع ، والبصر ، والكلام ، وتأويل الخبرية كالوجه واليدين والقدم والساق ونحو ذلك والحال الثالث : إثبات ذلك كله من غير تكييف ولا تشبيه جرياً على منوال السلف ، وهي طريقته في الإبانة التي صنفها آخراً .
And power, will, hearing, sight, speech, and the interpretation of the khabari attributes like the face, hands, foot, shin and so on. And the third state: affirming all of that without takyif (modality) nor tashbih (similitude), following the path of the salaf, and this is his method in al-Ibanah which he authored later.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage describes the three states (al-ahwal al-thalath) regarding the divine attributes. First, it mentions the attributes of power, will, hearing, sight, speech, and the interpretation of the khabari attributes such as face, hands, foot, shin. Then it states the third state: affirming all these attributes without asking how (takyif) or making any likeness (tashbih), following the way of the Salaf. This is the approach of al-Ash'ari in his book al-Ibanah, which he wrote later in his life. The passage emphasizes that the correct methodology is to affirm the attributes without delving into modality or anthropomorphism.

Key Terms
تأويل الخبرية
تكييف
تشبيه
السلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that affirming the attributes of God necessarily implies likening Him to creation (tashbih).
Correction: Al-Ash'ari clarifies that we affirm all attributes without takyif (asking 'how') and without tashbih (making any likeness), thus avoiding both extremes.

Checkpoint
What is the third state regarding divine attributes according to this passage?
A) Rejecting all attributes
B) Affirming attributes with interpretation
C) Affirming all attributes without modality or similitude
D) Denying the khabari attributes

Key Takeaway
The correct approach to divine attributes is to affirm them without modality or similitude, following the Salaf.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read verses about Allah's hand or face, do you feel a temptation to visualize them? How does the Salaf's principle of affirming without takyif challenge that instinct, and what will you do to train your heart to accept this without mental images?
?
The passage says to follow the path of the Salaf 'jari'an ala minwal al-salaf'. Is there an attribute of Allah that you find personally difficult to affirm without secretly comparing it to creation? Take a moment to identify that attribute, and commit to repeating 'I affirm it as Allah described, without how or likeness' every time your mind drifts.
?
If someone accused you of committing tashbih simply because you affirm the attributes literally, how would you respond using the exact language of this passage? And more importantly, is your own heart settled on this method, or do you still harbor doubts that need to be resolved with sincerity before Allah?

Al-Ash'ari on the Reality of the Qur'an's Multiple Modes
Al-Ash'ari's response on the Qur'an's real existence in multiple modes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari affirms that the Qur'an is truly present in the Preserved Tablet, in hearts, recited by tongues, written in copies, and heard by ears, while maintaining it is the uncreated speech of Allah.

Core Idea
The Qur'an is really in the Tablet, hearts, tongues, and copies—all without being created.

This passage from al-Bayhaqi's 'Al-I'tiqad' quotes Imam al-Ash'ari from his work 'Al-Ibanah' to clarify the nature of the Qur'an. Al-Ash'ari responds to a question about the Qur'an's location by affirming its real presence in multiple modes: the Preserved Tablet, the hearts of scholars, recited words, written copies, and audible sounds. This shows that the Qur'an's uncreated reality does not contradict its tangible manifestations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation to get the full context of al-Ash'ari's argument.
Notice the chain of transmission: al-Bayhaqi quoting al-Ash'ari.
2
Identify the question and answer
Find the question posed to al-Ash'ari: 'Do you say that God's speech is in the Preserved Tablet?' and note how he answers with a clear 'Yes' and provides evidence.
3
List the five modes of existence
Al-Ash'ari mentions five ways the Qur'an exists in reality: in the Preserved Tablet, in hearts, recited by tongues, written in copies, and heard by ears. List them and note the Quranic proofs for each.
The phrase 'in reality' (fi al-haqiqah) is key.
4
Examine the Quranic proofs
For each mode, al-Ash'ari cites a verse: Qur'an 85:21-22 for the Tablet, 20:114 for recitation, and 9:6 for hearing. Reflect on how these verses support his point.
The verse for hearts and writing is implied from the overall argument.
5
Understand the underlying doctrine
Al-Ash'ari's affirmation counters the idea that the Qur'an becomes created when recited or written. He maintains it is uncreated yet truly present in these created forms.
This is a key Sunni position against those who claimed the recited Qur'an is created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وممن عزا الإبانة إلى أبي الحسن الأشعري ، الحافظ الكبير أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين بن علي البيهقي الشافعي المتوفى سنة ٤٥٨ هـ . قال في كتاب « الاعتقاد والهداية إلى سبيل الرشاد » في باب القول في القرآن صفحة ٣١ : ذكر الشافعي رحمه الله ما دل على أن ما نتلوه من القرآن بألسنتنا ونسمعه بآذاننا ، ونكتبه في مصاحفنا يسمى كلام الله عز وجل ، وأن الله عز وجل كلم به عباده بأن أرسل به رسوله ، وبمعناه ذكره أيضاً علي بن إسماعيل في كتاب الإبانة . وقال في صفحة ٣٢ من الكتاب المذكور آنفاً : قال أبو الحسن علي بن إسماعيل في كتابه ، يعني الإبانة : فإن قال قائل : حدثونا ، تقولون إن كلام الله عز وجل في اللوح المحفوظ ، قيل له : نقول ذلك ، لأن الله قال : ﴿ بَلْ هُوَ قُرْآنٌ مَجِيدٌ * فِي لَوْحٍ مَحْفُوظٍ ﴾ فالقرآن في اللوح المحفوظ وهو في صدور الذين أوتوا العلم ، وهو متلو بالألسنة ، قال تعالى : ﴿ لَا تُحَرِّكْ بِهِ لِسَانَكَ ﴾ والقرآن مكتوب في مصاحفنا في الحقيقة ، محفوظ في صدورنا في الحقيقة ، متلو بألسنتنا في الحقيقة ، مسموع لنا في الحقيقة ، كما قال تعالى : ﴿ فَأَجِرْهُ حَتَّى يَسْمَعَ كَلَامَ اللَّهِ ﴾ ثم قال : في صفحة ٢٦ بعد سرد الأدلة على أن القرآن كلام الله غير مخلوق وقد احتج علي بن إسماعيل الأشعري رحمه الله تعالى بهذه الفصول . اهـ.
Among those who attributed al-Ibanah to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is the great hafiz Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn ibn 'Ali al-Bayhaqi al-Shafi'i, who died in 458 AH. He said in his book 'Al-I'tiqad wa al-Hidayah ila Sabil al-Rashad', in the chapter on the statement about the Qur'an, page 31: Al-Shafi'i, may God have mercy on him, mentioned what indicates that what we recite of the Qur'an with our tongues, hear with our ears, and write in our copies is called the speech of God Almighty, and that God Almighty spoke to His servants by sending His messenger with it. 'Ali ibn Isma'il also mentioned its meaning in the book al-Ibanah. And he said on page 32 of the aforementioned book: Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Isma'il said in his book, meaning al-Ibanah: If a questioner says: Tell us, do you say that the speech of God Almighty is in the Preserved Tablet? It is said to him: We say that, because God said: 'Nay, it is a glorious Qur'an, in a Preserved Tablet.' So the Qur'an is in the Preserved Tablet, and it is in the chests of those who have been given knowledge, and it is recited by tongues. God Almighty said: 'Move not your tongue with it.' And the Qur'an is written in our copies in reality, preserved in our chests in reality, recited by our tongues in reality, heard by us in reality, as God Almighty said: 'So grant him protection until he hears the speech of God.' Then he said on page 26, after citing the proofs that the Qur'an is the uncreated speech of God: And 'Ali ibn Isma'il al-Ash'ari, may God have mercy on him, adduced these sections. End.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a direct textual citation from al-Bayhaqi’s book 'Al-I'tiqad' confirming that al-Ash'ari's work 'Al-Ibanah' is authentic. Al-Bayhaqi first reports that al-Shafi'i held that the recited Qur'an is God’s speech. Then he quotes al-Ash'ari from 'Al-Ibanah' answering an objection: Some ask, 'Do you say God’s speech is in the Preserved Tablet?' Al-Ash'ari affirms this, citing Qur'an 85:21-22. He then expands: The Qur'an is both in the Preserved Tablet and in the hearts of scholars; it is recited by tongues, written in copies, and heard by ears—all in a real sense (fi al-haqiqah). He supports this with Qur'an 20:114 (about moving the tongue) and 9:6 (about hearing God’s speech). Al-Bayhaqi concludes that al-Ash'ari used these sections to argue that the Qur'an is uncreated speech. This passage thus shows al-Ash'ari's position on the reality of the Qur'an's multiple modes while maintaining its uncreatedness.

Key Terms
الإبانة
كلام الله
اللوح المحفوظ
غير مخلوق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari taught that the Qur'an is only in heaven and not truly recited or heard.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari explicitly states the Qur'an is 'in reality' recited, written, and heard, while remaining uncreated.

Checkpoint
According to the quote from al-Ibanah, where does al-Ash'ari say the Qur'an is located?
A) Only in heaven
B) In the Preserved Tablet, in hearts, recited, written, and heard
C) Only in the hearts of believers
D) Only in written form

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari affirms that the Qur'an, while being uncreated, truly exists in the Preserved Tablet, hearts, recitation, writing, and hearing—all in reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pick up a copy of the Qur'an, do you truly believe you are holding the uncreated speech of the Lord of the worlds in your hands? How would your reverence for that physical object change if you were to act on that belief consistently?
?
If the Qur'an is 'preserved in your chest in reality' (ḥāfiẓun fī ṣudūrinā fī al-ḥaqīqah), then why do you sometimes find it difficult to recall verses when you need them? What does that reveal about the state of your heart's connection to Allah's speech?
?
When you recite the Qur'an with your tongue in ṣalāh, do you ever pause and reflect that the very same words are being said by you, the created, yet are the uncreated words of the Creator? What would it take for you to feel that awe every time you begin to recite?

The Methodology of Ahl al-Sunnah
Imam al-Ash'ari answers a hypothetical objector by defining the methodology of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari defines the methodology of Ahl al-Sunnah as adherence to the Quran, the Sunnah, and the way of the Salaf, particularly Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal.

Core Idea
Ahl al-Sunnah's method is to cling to revelation and the transmitted way of the Salaf.

Imam al-Ash'ari begins his chapter by anticipating an objection: if you reject the positions of the heretical sects, then what is your own position? His response is not a speculative theology but a statement of adherence to the Quran, the Sunnah, and the path of the Companions and the imams of Hadith, embodied by Ahmad ibn Hanbal. This establishes the traditionalist foundation of Ash'ari theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the passage from 'فإن قال لنا قائل' to 'مفخم'. Notice the list of sects named in the objection.
2
Identify the sources of authority
In the response, find the three sources Ahl al-Sunnah cling to: the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Prophet, and what is narrated from the Companions, Followers, and imams of Hadith.
3
Reflect on the role of Ahmad ibn Hanbal
Consider why Imam al-Ash'ari specifically aligns with Ahmad ibn Hanbal. Notice the praise given and how it underscores the Salafi methodology.
This shows that Ash'ari theology is rooted in traditionalism, not rationalism alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في إبانة قول أهل الحق والسنة

فإن قال لنا قائل : قد أنكرتم قول المعتزلة والقدرية والجهمية والحرورية والرافضة والمرجئة ، فعرفونا قولكم الذي تقولون وديانتكم التي بها تدينون . قيل له : قولنا الذي نقول به وديانتنا التي ندين بها التمسك بكتاب ربنا عز وجل وسنة نبينا عليه السلام وما روي عن الصحابة والتابعين وأئمة الحديث ، ونحن بذلك معتصمون ، وبما كان يقول به أبو عبد الله أحمد بن محمد بن حنبل نضر الله وجهه ورفع درجته وأجزل مثوبته قائلون ، ولما خالف قوله مخالفون ، لأنه الإمام الفاضل والرئيس الكامل الذي أبان الله به الحق ورفع به الضلال وأوضح به المنهاج وقمع به بدع المبتدعين وزيغ الزائغين وشك الشاكين فرحمة الله عليه من إمام مقدم وجليل معظم مفخم .

وجملة قولنا إنا نقر بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله وبما جاءوا به من عند الله وما رواه الثقات عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا نرد من ذلك شيئاً .

وأن الله عز وجل إله واحد لا إله إلا هو فرد صمد لم يتخذ صاحبة ولا ولداً .

وأن محمداً عبده ورسوله أرسله بالهدى ودين الحق ، وأن الساعة آتية لا ريب فيها

وأن الله يبعث من في القبور ، وأن الله مستو على عرشه كما قال : الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى .
A chapter on clarifying the statement of the people of truth and the Sunnah. If someone says to us: You have rejected the statement of the Mu'tazila, Qadariyya, Jahmiyya, Haruriyya, Rafida, and Murji'a. So inform us of your statement that you say and your religion with which you practice. It is said to him: Our statement that we say and our religion with which we practice is adherence to the Book of our Lord, Mighty and Majestic, and the Sunnah of our Prophet, peace be upon him, and what has been narrated from the Companions, the Followers, and the imams of Hadith. And we cling to that. And we are followers of what Abu Abdullah Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Hanbal (may Allah brighten his face, raise his rank, and increase his reward) used to say, and we oppose those who oppose his statement. Because he is the virtuous imam, the perfect leader, through whom Allah manifested the truth, removed misguidance, clarified the methodology, and suppressed the innovations of the innovators, the deviations of the deviators, and the doubts of the doubters. May Allah's mercy be upon him, a foremost imam, a great and honored noble. And the summary of our statement is that we affirm Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, and what they brought from Allah, and what the trustworthy have narrated from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him); we reject none of that. And that Allah, Mighty and Majestic, is one God, there is no god but He, unique, eternal, who has not taken a companion nor a son. And that Muhammad is His servant and messenger; He sent him with guidance and the religion of truth. And that the Hour is coming, no doubt in it. And that Allah will resurrect those in the graves. And that Allah is established upon His Throne as He said: 'The Most Merciful established upon the Throne.'
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a creedal statement from Imam al-Ash'ari that opens a chapter dedicated to clarifying the doctrine of Ahl al-Haqq wa al-Sunnah. It begins with a hypothetical objector who notes that the Ash'ari's have rejected the positions of various heretical sects (Mu'tazila, Qadariyya, etc.) and demands a clear exposition of their own belief. The answer first defines their methodology: adherence to the Quran, the Sunnah of the Prophet, and the transmitted reports from the Companions, Followers, and imams of Hadith. They specifically align themselves with the teachings of Ahmad ibn Hanbal, praising him as the imam through whom Allah manifested truth and suppressed innovation. This establishes a traditionalist, Salafi methodology. Then follows a concise summary of beliefs (جملة قولنا): affirmation of Allah, angels, books, messengers, and all authentic traditions without rejection; the oneness of Allah, negating any partner or child; the prophethood of Muhammad; the certainty of the Hour; the resurrection of the dead; and the divine attribute of istiwa (being established upon the Throne) as stated in the Quran without interpretation. The passage thus presents the core Ash'ari creed as one of affirming revelation and the attributes of Allah as they are reported, in line with the Salaf.

Key Terms
أهل الحق والسنة
التمسك بكتاب الله وسنة نبيه
أحمد بن حنبل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Ash'ari school is based solely on rational theology and not on the Salafi method.
Correction: This passage shows that al-Ash'ari explicitly defines his school's methodology as adherence to Quran, Sunnah, and the way of the Salaf, especially Ahmad ibn Hanbal.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what are the three sources of authority that Ahl al-Sunnah cling to?
A) The Quran, the Sunnah, and the sayings of the Salaf
B) The Quran, reason, and consensus
C) The Quran, the Sunnah, and the opinions of the Mu'tazila
D) The Quran, the Sunnah, and the teachings of the Rafida

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunnah's method is to adhere strictly to the Quran, Sunnah, and the way of the Salaf, as exemplified by Imam Ahmad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly measure every belief and action by the Quran and Sunnah, or do you allow your desires, culture, or peer pressure to shape your faith? Before Sunday ends, identify one area where you have compromised and repent.
?
Imam al-Ash'ari proudly declared his allegiance to Imam Ahmad. Is there any scholar or pious predecessor whose way you follow with such conviction? If not, why are you hesitant? Ask Allah to grant you a guide to the truth.
?
When someone asks you about your religion, do you answer with clear texts like this passage, or do you defend your own opinions? Tonight, write down your personal creed and compare it to the sources mentioned here—where do they differ?

The Core Creed of Ahl al-Sunnah
Imam al-Ash'ari enumerates the core beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will know the essential articles of faith affirmed by Ahl al-Sunnah as summarized by Imam al-Ash'ari.

Core Idea
The creed of Ahl al-Sunnah is to affirm all that Allah and His Messenger have told us, without rejection or interpretation.

After establishing the methodology of relying on revelation and the Salaf, Imam al-Ash'ari provides a concise summary of the beliefs held by Ahl al-Sunnah. This summary covers the fundamentals: belief in Allah, angels, books, messengers, the afterlife, and the divine attribute of istiwa as stated in the Quran. It is a straightforward affirmation of what has been reported from the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the summary statement
Read the passage from 'وجملة قولنا' to the end. Notice how it begins with a general affirmation and then lists specific beliefs.
2
Identify each item affirmed
List all the beliefs mentioned: affirmation of Allah, angels, books, messengers, etc. Also note the phrase 'لا نرد من ذلك شيئاً' (we reject none of that).
3
Focus on the attribute of istiwa
Notice that the passage ends with the verse 'الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى' and says 'كما قال' (as He said). This shows that Ahl al-Sunnah affirm the attribute without ta'wil.
This refutes the claim that al-Ash'ari denied the literal meaning of istiwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في إبانة قول أهل الحق والسنة

فإن قال لنا قائل : قد أنكرتم قول المعتزلة والقدرية والجهمية والحرورية والرافضة والمرجئة ، فعرفونا قولكم الذي تقولون وديانتكم التي بها تدينون . قيل له : قولنا الذي نقول به وديانتنا التي ندين بها التمسك بكتاب ربنا عز وجل وسنة نبينا عليه السلام وما روي عن الصحابة والتابعين وأئمة الحديث ، ونحن بذلك معتصمون ، وبما كان يقول به أبو عبد الله أحمد بن محمد بن حنبل نضر الله وجهه ورفع درجته وأجزل مثوبته قائلون ، ولما خالف قوله مخالفون ، لأنه الإمام الفاضل والرئيس الكامل الذي أبان الله به الحق ورفع به الضلال وأوضح به المنهاج وقمع به بدع المبتدعين وزيغ الزائغين وشك الشاكين فرحمة الله عليه من إمام مقدم وجليل معظم مفخم .

وجملة قولنا إنا نقر بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله وبما جاءوا به من عند الله وما رواه الثقات عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا نرد من ذلك شيئاً .

وأن الله عز وجل إله واحد لا إله إلا هو فرد صمد لم يتخذ صاحبة ولا ولداً .

وأن محمداً عبده ورسوله أرسله بالهدى ودين الحق ، وأن الساعة آتية لا ريب فيها

وأن الله يبعث من في القبور ، وأن الله مستو على عرشه كما قال : الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى .
A chapter on clarifying the statement of the people of truth and the Sunnah. If someone says to us: You have rejected the statement of the Mu'tazila, Qadariyya, Jahmiyya, Haruriyya, Rafida, and Murji'a. So inform us of your statement that you say and your religion with which you practice. It is said to him: Our statement that we say and our religion with which we practice is adherence to the Book of our Lord, Mighty and Majestic, and the Sunnah of our Prophet, peace be upon him, and what has been narrated from the Companions, the Followers, and the imams of Hadith. And we cling to that. And we are followers of what Abu Abdullah Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Hanbal (may Allah brighten his face, raise his rank, and increase his reward) used to say, and we oppose those who oppose his statement. Because he is the virtuous imam, the perfect leader, through whom Allah manifested the truth, removed misguidance, clarified the methodology, and suppressed the innovations of the innovators, the deviations of the deviators, and the doubts of the doubters. May Allah's mercy be upon him, a foremost imam, a great and honored noble. And the summary of our statement is that we affirm Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, and what they brought from Allah, and what the trustworthy have narrated from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him); we reject none of that. And that Allah, Mighty and Majestic, is one God, there is no god but He, unique, eternal, who has not taken a companion nor a son. And that Muhammad is His servant and messenger; He sent him with guidance and the religion of truth. And that the Hour is coming, no doubt in it. And that Allah will resurrect those in the graves. And that Allah is established upon His Throne as He said: 'The Most Merciful established upon the Throne.'
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a creedal statement from Imam al-Ash'ari that opens a chapter dedicated to clarifying the doctrine of Ahl al-Haqq wa al-Sunnah. It begins with a hypothetical objector who notes that the Ash'ari's have rejected the positions of various heretical sects (Mu'tazila, Qadariyya, etc.) and demands a clear exposition of their own belief. The answer first defines their methodology: adherence to the Quran, the Sunnah of the Prophet, and the transmitted reports from the Companions, Followers, and imams of Hadith. They specifically align themselves with the teachings of Ahmad ibn Hanbal, praising him as the imam through whom Allah manifested truth and suppressed innovation. This establishes a traditionalist, Salafi methodology. Then follows a concise summary of beliefs (جملة قولنا): affirmation of Allah, angels, books, messengers, and all authentic traditions without rejection; the oneness of Allah, negating any partner or child; the prophethood of Muhammad; the certainty of the Hour; the resurrection of the dead; and the divine attribute of istiwa (being established upon the Throne) as stated in the Quran without interpretation. The passage thus presents the core Ash'ari creed as one of affirming revelation and the attributes of Allah as they are reported, in line with the Salaf.

Key Terms
جملة القول
استوى على العرش
لا نرد من ذلك شيئاً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that al-Ash'ari denied the literal meaning of istiwa and interpreted it as 'istila' (conquering).
Correction: This passage shows that al-Ash'ari explicitly affirms istiwa as Allah said, without ta'wil, using the phrase 'كما قال' (as He said).

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the stance of Ahl al-Sunnah regarding reports from the trustworthy narrators from the Prophet?
A) They reject some that contradict reason.
B) They accept them all without rejection.
C) They only accept what is in the Quran.
D) They interpret them allegorically.

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunnah affirm all divine attributes as revealed, including istiwa, without rejection or figurative interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly affirm every single thing Allah and His Messenger have told us, even those that clash with your desires or modern sensibilities? Which teachings do you find hardest to accept without reservation?
?
If you were asked to give a summary of your faith starting with 'the summary of our statement is that we affirm...', could you list the core beliefs without hesitation? What would that reveal about the state of your iman?
?
The resurrection is certain—are you living today as if you will stand before Allah? If the Hour came right now, what would you wish you had done differently? Write down one concrete action you will take today to prepare.

The Believers Will See Allah in the Hereafter
Al-Ash'ari affirms believers will see Allah with their eyes in Paradise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni belief in the vision of Allah (ru'ya) in the Hereafter, supported by hadith and Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Believers will see Allah with their eyes in Paradise, just as clearly as the full moon.

Imam al-Ash'ari begins by affirming a core Sunni belief: that Allah will be seen by the believers in the Hereafter. He supports this with a prophetic analogy and contrasts it with the veiling of disbelievers. He also recounts the story of Prophet Musa to show that this vision is exclusive to the afterlife.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation to get the literal meaning.
Pay attention to the analogy of the full moon.
2
Identify the three parts
The passage has three distinct assertions: (a) affirmation of vision, (b) veiling of disbelievers, (c) the story of Musa. Notice how each is supported.
3
Reflect on the theological implications
Consider why the full moon analogy is used and what the Musa story teaches about the limitation of vision in this world.
This vision is a real, physical sight, not metaphorical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وندين بأن الله تعالى يرى في الآخرة بالأبصار كما يرى القمر ليلة البدر يراه المؤمنون كما جاءت الروايات عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. ونقول : أن الكافرين محجوبون عنه إذا رآه المؤمنون في الجنة ، كما قال عز وجل : كَلَّا إِنَّهُمْ عَن رَّبِّهِمْ يَوْمَذٍ مَحْجُوبُونَ ﴾ وأن موسى عليه السلام سأل الله عز وجل الرؤية في الدنيا ، وأن الله سبحانه تجلى للجبل فجعله دكاً ، فأعلم بذلك موسى أنه لا يراه في الدنيا
And we hold as religion that Allah the Exalted will be seen in the Hereafter with the eyes, as the moon is seen on the night of the full moon; the believers will see Him, as the narrations came from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. And we say: that the disbelievers are veiled from Him when the believers see Him in Paradise, as He said, Mighty and Majestic: 'No! Indeed, they will be veiled from their Lord that Day.' And that Musa, peace be upon him, asked Allah, Mighty and Majestic, for vision in this world, and that Allah, glorified be He, manifested to the mountain and made it leveled, and thereby informed Musa that he would not see Him in this world.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the belief in the vision of Allah (ru'ya) in the afterlife. It begins by asserting that Allah will be seen by the eyes in the Hereafter, using the analogy of seeing the full moon—a well-known hadith. The vision is a special blessing for the believers. The disbelievers, however, will be veiled from their Lord, as stated in the Quran (Surah Al-Mutaffifin, verse 15). The passage then recounts the story of Prophet Musa (Moses) who asked to see Allah in this world. Allah responded by manifesting His glory to the mountain, which crumbled, thereby teaching Musa that He cannot be seen in this worldly life. Thus, the vision is exclusively for the Hereafter.

حجاب
تجلى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some deny the literal vision of Allah in the Hereafter, viewing it as metaphorical.
Correction: Imam al-Ash'ari affirms it as a real, physical sight for believers in Paradise, supported by hadith and Quran.

Checkpoint

D) Musa saw Allah briefly.

Key Takeaway
The vision of Allah in the Hereafter is a real, physical sight for believers, a blessing denied to disbelievers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You long for the vision of Allah in Paradise, but what if you are among the veiled? Look at your life now: are you living in a way that seeks Allah's pleasure, or do you prefer the veils of this world? Commit to one change today that removes a veil between you and your Lord.
?
Prophet Musa asked to see Allah in this world, but it was not granted. Are you impatient for what Allah has decreed for the Hereafter? Do you demand signs or experiences now? Surrender your desire for immediate gratification and trust that the vision is reserved for the right time.
?
The believers will see Allah as clearly as the moon. Does that hope fill your heart with longing and action? Or does it feel distant? Write one concrete act that you will do this week to increase your love for meeting your Lord.

Affirming Divine Attributes from Hadith
Al-Ash'ari affirms two hadith-based divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari affirms two specific divine attributes reported in hadith—Allah turning hearts between two fingers and placing the heavens on a finger—without figurative interpretation.

Core Idea
Divine attributes from hadith are affirmed as real, not metaphorical.

Al-Ash'ari presents two distinct attributes of Allah that are explicitly mentioned in authentic hadith. These passages are not to be interpreted allegorically; rather, they are accepted as they came, while negating any resemblance to creation. This lesson examines the two affirmations and the underlying methodology of accepting scriptural reports literally in matters of divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully. Notice the phrase 'بين أصبعين' and 'على إصبع'. These are key terms.
The dual form 'أصبعين' (two fingers) is used for hearts, and singular 'إصبع' for heavens/earths.
2
Identify the two affirmations
Find the two separate claims: (1) Allah turns hearts between two fingers, (2) Allah places heavens and earth on a finger, and earths on a finger.
Each is introduced by 'بأن' after the initial declaration of belief.
3
Understand the methodology
Al-Ash'ari states these 'as the narration came'—meaning he accepts the reports without ta'wil (figurative interpretation). This is key to his approach.
The Ash'ari school affirms attributes in a manner befitting Allah, negating anthropomorphism (tashbih).
4
Address the common misconception
Some claim these are metaphors. Al-Ash'ari rejects this, affirming the literal wording while negating any human-like quality.
This balances textual fidelity with transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وندين الله عز وجل بأنه يقلب القلوب بين أصبعين من أصابع الله عز وجل. وأنه عز وجل يضع السموات والأرض على إصبع والأرضين على إصبع كما جاءت الرواية عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم
And we hold as religion regarding Allah, Mighty and Majestic, that He turns the hearts between two fingers of the fingers of Allah, Mighty and Majestic. And that He, Mighty and Majestic, places the heavens and the earth on a finger, and the earths on a finger, as the narration came from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage affirms two specific attributes of Allah mentioned in authentic hadith. First, that Allah turns the hearts of people between two of His fingers, meaning He has complete control over the hearts' state—guidance or misguidance. This is based on the famous hadith: 'The hearts of the children of Adam are between two fingers of the Merciful's fingers.' Second, that on the Day of Resurrection, Allah will place the heavens and the earth on a finger, and the earths (plural, referring to the seven earths) on another finger, as narrated in hadith about the Day of Judgment. The Ash'ari methodology is to accept these reports as they are without figurative interpretation (ta'wil), affirming that Allah has fingers in a manner befitting His majesty, while negating any likeness to creation.

Key Terms
قلب
إصبع
وضع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that the phrases 'two fingers' and 'on a finger' are merely metaphors for power or control, not real attributes.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari affirms them as real attributes of Allah, accepted as they came in the hadith, without interpreting them figuratively.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the basis for affirming that Allah places the heavens on a finger?
A) It is derived from rational argument.
B) It is based on a narration from the Prophet.
C) It is a metaphor for power.
D) It is a statement of the Salaf.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari affirms divine attributes from hadith literally while maintaining transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your heart is between the fingers of Allah, that He can turn it to guidance or misguidance in an instant? How does this truth shape your daily prayers for steadfastness? Will you today pause and ask Allah to keep your heart firm upon His path?
?
Knowing that Allah will place the heavens and earth on a finger on the Day of Resurrection, how does this image affect your fear of His power and your hope in His mercy? Does it make you more conscious of your accountability? What will you do to prepare for that day?
?
If you have ever felt your heart harden or drift, have you remembered that Allah alone controls its turning? What will you do today to ask Him to turn it back to obedience? Will you make a sincere du'a right now?

Affirming Divine Descent and the Method of Ahl al-Sunnah
Affirmation of divine descent and statement of Sunni methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari affirms narrated divine attributes and establishes the Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus as the sources for resolving theological disagreements.

Core Idea
Ahl al-Sunnah accept transmitted divine attributes and resolve disputes through revelation and consensus.

Imam al-Ash'ari now turns from refuting false beliefs to positively stating the position of Ahl al-Sunnah. He affirms the narrated reports about Allah's descent and His speech, and then lays down the fundamental principle for settling all theological differences: the Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus. This concise statement captures both the content and the methodology of Sunni orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage attentively
Read the Arabic original and its translation. Notice that the passage has two clear parts: an affirmation of specific narrated reports about Allah, and a general methodological rule for resolving disagreements.
The first part directly counters those who deny attributes like descent.
2
Identify the key affirmations
Look for what exactly is affirmed: descent to the lowest heaven, Allah's saying 'Is there anyone asking?' and all other matters transmitted by the people of transmission. Understand that this is a blanket acceptance of authentic narrations about divine acts.
3
Analyze the methodology
Examine the three sources given for resolving differences: the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Prophet, and the consensus of the Muslims. Also note the prohibition of innovation and speaking without knowledge.
This is a classic statement of the Sunni legal and theological methodology.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why the Imam begins with descent before stating the methodology. This shows that accepting transmitted reports is an act of following revelation, not rational speculation. The methodology then guards against both innovation and denial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونصدق جميع الروايات التي يثبتها أهل النقل من النزول إلى السماء الدنيا، وأن الرب عز وجل يقول: هل من سائل، هل من مستغفر، وبسائر ما نقلوه وأثبتوه خلافاً لما قال أهل الزيغ والتضليل. ونعول فيما اختلفنا فيه على كتاب ربنا وسنة نبينا وإجماع المسلمين وما كان في معناه. ولا نبتدع في دين الله ما لم يأذن لنا، ولا نقول على الله ما لا نعلم.
And we affirm the truth of all the narrations that the people of transmission establish regarding the descent to the lowest heaven, and that the Lord, Mighty and Majestic, says: 'Is there anyone asking? Is there anyone seeking forgiveness?' and all other matters that they have transmitted and established, contrary to what the people of deviation and misguidance say. And we rely, in matters in which we differ, upon the Book of our Lord, the Sunnah of our Prophet, and the consensus of the Muslims, and what is in accordance with them. And we do not innovate in the religion of Allah that which He has not permitted us, nor do we say about Allah that which we do not know.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a creedal affirmation regarding divine attributes and methodology. It begins by asserting belief in the narrated reports about Allah's descent to the lowest heaven and His saying 'Is there anyone asking?' etc. This is in opposition to those who deny such attributes (Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya). Then it states the principle of resolving disagreements: relying on Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus, and not innovating or speaking about Allah without knowledge.

Key Terms
النزول إلى السماء الدنيا
أهل النقل
أهل الزيغ والتضليل
إجماع المسلمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ash'aris reject all literal meanings of divine attributes, including narrations about descent.
Correction: Imam al-Ash'ari explicitly affirms the narrated reports of descent and Allah's speech, showing that Sunnis accept them without ta'wil (allegorical interpretation) when authentically transmitted. The methodology ensures these are understood in a way befitting Allah's majesty.

Checkpoint

A) They should be interpreted metaphorically
B) They are all false
C) We affirm them as true
D) We remain silent about them

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunnah affirm authentic narrated reports about Allah's attributes and resolve all differences through the Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Are you quick to speak about Allah's attributes or actions without certain knowledge? How can you train yourself to say 'I do not know' before you speak?
?
When you encounter a theological disagreement, do you instinctively search for what the Qur'an and Sunnah say, or do you lean on what is popular or comfortable? Which of these habits will you commit to changing today?

Affirming God's Coming and Nearness
The author affirms God's coming and nearness from the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari school affirms the attributes of divine coming and nearness as literal events, supported by Quranic verses, while avoiding modality (bila kayf).

Core Idea
Allah's coming and nearness are true events, known from the Quran, but their 'how' is unknown.

This passage from Imam al-Ash'ari's al-Ibanah establishes a key principle of Sunni creed: we affirm what Allah and His Messenger have said about His actions, without questioning the modality. Here, the author focuses on two attributes—coming (maji') and nearness (qurb)—citing clear Quranic verses. As you read, notice how the author simply states the belief and supports it with scripture, avoiding any figurative interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let the author's own wording sink in.
2
Identify the two attributes affirmed
The passage affirms two divine actions: 'coming' on Judgment Day and 'nearness' to His servants. Find where each is mentioned.
These are distinct attributes, both mentioned in the Quran.
3
Note the three Quranic proofs
The author cites three verses: one for coming (Surah al-Fajr 22) and two for nearness (Surah Qaf 16, Surah an-Najm 8-9). See how each verse directly supports the claim.
4
Understand the principle of bila kayf
The phrase 'كيف شاء' (however He wills) shows the Ash'ari method of affirming without specifying modality. This is a core principle.
Bila kayf means we do not ask 'how'.
5
Connect to broader methodology
This passage exemplifies the salafi method of affirming attributes as they appear, without ta'wil (figurative interpretation). Reflect on why this is important.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونقول: إن الله عز وجل يجيء يوم القيامة كما قال: {وَجَاءَ رَبُّكَ وَالْمَلَكُ صَفّاً صَفّاً}. وأن الله عز وجل يقرب من عباده كيف شاء كما قال: {وَنَحْنُ أَقْرَبُ إِلَيْهِ مِنْ حَبْلِ الْوَرِيدِ} وكما قال: {ثُمَّ دَنَا فَتَدَلَّى * فَكَانَ قَابَ قَوْسَيْنِ أَوْ أَدْنَى}.
And we say: Indeed Allah, Mighty and Majestic, will come on the Day of Resurrection as He said: 'And your Lord comes, and the angels, rank upon rank.' And that Allah, Mighty and Majestic, draws near to His servants however He wills, as He said: 'And We are nearer to him than the jugular vein,' and as He said: 'Then He approached and descended, and was at a distance of two bow-lengths or nearer.'
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage affirms the reality of divine actions of coming and nearness as described in the Qur'an, without specifying modality (bila kayf). It cites three verses: Surah al-Fajr 22 about coming, Surah Qaf 16 about nearness, and Surah an-Najm 8-9 about the Prophet's closeness to Allah during the Ascension. The belief is that these are true, and it rejects metaphorical interpretations that negate the literal meaning.

القرب
الكيف

Key Takeaway

?

Ash'ari's Creed on Divine Knowledge and Obedience
Ash'ari enumerates three creedal affirmations: divine knowledge, obedience, and avoidance of innovation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core Sunni creedal affirmations regarding God's omniscience, obedience to Muslim leaders, and separation from innovators as articulated by Imam al-Ash'ari.

Core Idea
Ash'ari's creed centres on God's exhaustive knowledge and the duty to follow the sunna.

This passage from al-Ash'ari's al-Ibanah is a concise statement of fundamental Sunni beliefs. It opens with a declaration of faith in God's comprehensive knowledge covering all possibilities, then moves to practical commitments: obedience to Muslim leaders and avoidance of innovators. These three principles form a cornerstone of classical Sunni identity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Notice the opening verb 'نَدِين' which signals a creedal declaration.
2
Identify the three creedal statements
The passage presents three distinct affirmations. Find each one: God's knowledge, obedience to leaders, and avoiding innovators.
3
Analyze the scope of God's knowledge
Consider the phrases 'ما كان وما يكون وما لا يكون أن لو كان كيف كان يكون'. This affirms God knows even hypotheticals.
This shows God's knowledge is not limited to actual events.
4
Reflect on practical obligations
The second and third statements order obedience to leaders and separation from innovators. Think about why these are included in a creed.
This underscores that creed impacts community conduct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وندين الله عز وجل بأنه يعلم ما العباد عاملون وإلى ما هم صائرون ، وما كان وما يكون وما لا يكون أن لو كان كيف كان يكون وبطاعة الأئمة المسلمين، ونرى مفارقة كل داعية إلى بدعته ومجانبة أهل الهوى .
And we affirm as a religion unto God Almighty that He knows what the servants are doing and to what they are heading, and what was and what will be and what is not—[and] if it were, how it would be—and (we affirm) obedience to the Muslim leaders, and we consider abandoning every caller to his innovation and avoiding the people of desires.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a creedal declaration from Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's book al-Ibanah. It begins with the verb 'نَدِين' (we affirm as a religion), indicating that these statements are part of the religious creed. The first belief affirmed is God's comprehensive knowledge: He knows the actions of servants ('ما العباد عاملون'), their future destinations ('إلى ما هم صائرون'), and all temporal states—past, future, and even non-existent possibilities ('ما كان وما يكون وما لا يكون أن لو كان كيف كان يكون'). This establishes God's omniscience over all things, including hypotheticals. The second belief is obedience to the Muslim leaders (أئمة المسلمين), reflecting the Sunni teaching of obeying those in authority in lawful matters. The third is the duty to abandon every caller to innovation (داعية إلى بدعته) and avoid the people of desires (أهل الهوى), emphasizing the importance of preserving the sunna. This succinct statement encapsulates core Sunni convictions.

Key Terms
ندين
يعلم
الأئمة
بدعة
أهل الهوى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage implies blind obedience to any ruler, regardless of justice.
Correction: Obedience to leaders is conditioned by what is in accordance with Shariah, though not stated explicitly here; Sunni scholars require obedience in lawful matters.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the stance of Ahl al-Sunnah towards innovators?
A) Debate them politely
B) Abandon their call and avoid them
C) Love and respect them
D) Condemn them to death

Key Takeaway
This passage captures three foundational Sunni beliefs: God's absolute knowledge, obedience to legitimate leadership, and separation from innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson affirms that Allah knows every detail of your life, even the hypotheticals of what you would do if circumstances were different. Is there a secret sin or thought you have tried to hide, believing it would never be known? How does the reality of His exhaustive knowledge change your next moment of temptation? Will you confess it to Him now and resolve to abandon it?
?
The passage commands obedience to Muslim leaders. Think of the last time you were asked to obey an authority in your community—whether a parent, teacher, or imam. Did you obey from your heart, or did you resist because of your own desires? What is one practical step you can take today to cultivate genuine obedience to those in charge, even when it is difficult?
?
You are told to abandon every caller to innovation and avoid people of desires. Who in your life—online or in person—calls you to something that distracts you from the sunna? Is there a friend, influencer, or group whose influence you have been tolerating? What concrete action will you take this week to distance yourself from that influence, seeking instead the company of those who uphold the sunna?

Affirming Allah's Oneness and Transcendence
Imam Ash'ari praises Allah with names affirming oneness and transcendence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari opens his theological work by praising Allah's unique oneness, transcendence, and absolute will.

Core Idea
Allah is unique in His essence and attributes, beyond all comparison.

Imam al-Ash'ari begins his book with a profound doxology that establishes the foundation of his theology: Allah is absolutely one and unique, with no likeness or equal. This opening praise sets the stage for the entire discussion on divine attributes that follows.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening praise
Read the Arabic passage from 'الحمد لله الأحد الواحد' to 'الفعال لما يريد' once. Then read the translation. Notice the rhythmic and exalted language.
The passage uses a series of divine names and descriptions.
2
Identify key descriptors of Allah
List the attributes and names in the passage: الأحد, الواحد, العزيز, الماجد, المتفرد بالتوحيد, المتمجد بالتمجيد, المبدي المعيد, الفعال لما يريد. What do they emphasize?
These affirm unity, might, glory, and absolute will.
3
Reflect on the negation of comparison
Notice the phrase 'لا تبلغه صفات العبيد' and 'ليس له مثل ولا نديد'. These negate any similarity between Allah and creation. Why is this important for kalam?
This establishes Allah's transcendence (tanzih).
4
Connect to the lesson's core idea
Consider how this opening praise sets a clear theological boundary: Allah is beyond all human attributes and comparisons. This is the starting point for defending tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم و به نستعين وهو حسبي ونعم الوكيل قال السيد الشيخ الإمام العالم أبو الحسن علي بن إسماعيل بن علي ابن أبي بشر الأشعري البصري رحمه الله : ١ - الحمد لله الأحد الواحد، العزيز الماجد ، المتفرد بالتوحيد المتمجد بالتمجيد، الذي لا تبلغه صفات العبيد، ليس له مثل ولا نديد وهو المبدي المعيد، الفعال لما يريد، جل عن اتخاذ الصاحبة والأبناء وتقدس عن ملامسة النساء فليست له عثرة تقال، ولا حد يضرب له فيه المثال، لم يزل بصفاته أولاً قديراً ولا يزال عالماً خبيراً، سبق الأشياء علمه، ونفذت فيها إرادته، ولم تعرب عنه خفيات الأمور، ولم تغيره سوالف صروف الدهور، ولم يلحقه في خلق شيء مما خلق كلال ولا تعب، ولا مسه لغوب ولا نصب، خلق الأشياء بقدرته، ودبرها بمشيئته، وقهرها بجبروته، وذللها بعزته، فذل لعظمته المتكبرون، واستكان لعز ربوبيته المتعظمون
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. And with Him we seek help, and He is sufficient for me and the best disposer of affairs. The master, the sheikh, the imam, the scholar, Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ismail ibn Ali ibn Abi Bishr al-Ash'ari al-Basri, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 1 - Praise be to Allah, the One, the Unique, the Mighty, the Glorious, the one who is unique in oneness, the one who is glorified in glorification, whom the attributes of servants do not reach; He has no like nor equal, and He is the Originator and the Restorer, the Doer of whatever He wills. He is exalted above taking a companion and children, and sanctified above touching women. He has no slip that is mentioned, nor is there any limit that is struck for Him as an example. He has not ceased with His attributes, from eternity powerful, and He will not cease knowing and aware. His knowledge preceded all things, and His will executed in them. Hidden matters are not concealed from Him, nor do the changes of the times alter Him. No fatigue or weariness befalls Him in creating anything that He created, nor does weariness or exhaustion touch Him. He created things by His power, and arranged them by His will, and subdued them by His might, and humbled them by His strength. So the arrogant submit to His greatness, and the haughty become humble before the might of His Lordship.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is the opening doxology (khutbah) of Imam al-Ash'ari's book. It serves as a theological preamble, establishing the key attributes of Allah that form the foundation of his argument throughout the work. The author begins with the basmalah and seeking help from Allah, affirming his reliance on Him. He then introduces himself as Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. The praise (hamd) is directed to Allah, described with names and attributes that emphasize His uniqueness and transcendence. 'Al-Ahad al-Wahid' affirms absolute oneness; 'al-Aziz al-Majid' affirms might and glory; 'al-Mutafarrid bi al-tawhid' stresses that He alone is unique in His oneness. 'Al-Mutamajjid bi al-tamjid' indicates that He glorifies Himself. 'Lā tablughuhu ṣifāt al-'abīd' negates that any human attribute can reach or encompass Him. 'Laysa lahu mithlun wa lā nadīd' denies any likeness or equal. 'Al-Mubdi' al-Mu'īd' describes Him as the originator and restorer of creation. 'Al-Fa''āl limā yurīd' asserts His absolute will. Then the text negates any anthropomorphic or familial associations: exalted above taking a companion or children, sanctified from touching women. He has no mistake ('athra) and no limit (ḥadd) can be set for Him. He has always been with His attributes—eternally powerful, always knowing and aware. His knowledge preceded all things, and His will was executed in them. Nothing hidden escapes Him; time does not change Him. No fatigue or weariness touches Him in creation, affirming His power and self-sufficiency. He created by His power, arranged by His will, subdued by His might, and humbled by His strength. The passage concludes by noting the effect of these attributes: the arrogant become humbled. This doxology sets a clear course for Ash'ari's theology: it is intensely monotheistic, affirms eternal attributes, transcends anthropomorphism, and establishes Allah's absolute sovereignty. The phrasing anticipates later arguments against those who deny attributes (Mu'tazila) or those who overly anthropomorphize (Mujassima).

Key Terms
الأحد
الواحد
المبدي المعيد
الفعال لما يريد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the phrase 'لا تبلغه صفات العبيد' (whom the attributes of servants do not reach) teach about Allah?
A) Allah has attributes similar to humans
B) Allah's attributes are beyond human comprehension
C) Servants can describe Allah fully
D) Allah is limited by human understanding

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ash'ari opens by affirming that Allah is absolutely one, unique, and beyond all comparison, establishing the foundation of tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If no attribute of servants can reach Allah, then how do you approach Him in your du'a? Do you still try to describe Him with human categories, or do you stand in awe of His absolute transcendence? What will you change in your prayer tonight to reflect this truth?
?
You claim Allah is 'the Doer of whatever He wills' — but do you truly submit to His will in every area of your life? Is there a situation where you have resisted His decree because it clashed with your own desires? Will you now surrender that to Him?
?
The passage says 'He has no like nor equal.' Yet we often compare Allah to our limited understanding. When you think of Allah's mercy, justice, or power, are you tempted to measure them by human standards? How can you train your heart to affirm His uniqueness without reducing Him to your imagination? What specific step will you take today?

Negating Anthropomorphism and Affirming Eternal Attributes
Imam Ash'ari negates anthropomorphism and affirms Allah's eternal attributes and sovereignty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari rejects all human limitations from Allah and affirms His eternal attributes, knowledge, and power.

Core Idea
Allah is free from human imperfections and His attributes are eternal and unchanging.

In the second part of his opening doxology, Imam al-Ash'ari explicitly distances Allah from any human characteristics—such as having a family, making mistakes, or being limited by time—and then affirms that His attributes are eternal, His knowledge all-encompassing, and His power irresistible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic from 'جل عن اتخاذ الصاحبة والأبناء' to the end of the source chunk. Read the translation. Notice how the tone shifts from praise to negation and then to affirmation.
This section is more argumentative in style.
2
Identify the negations of human limitations
Find the phrases that negate Allah having a companion, children, touching women, making a mistake, or having a limit. List them.
Examples: 'جل عن اتخاذ الصاحبة والأبناء', 'تقدس عن ملامسة النساء', 'ليست له عثرة تقال', 'ولا حد يضرب له فيه المثال'.
3
Identify affirmations of eternal attributes
Find the phrases that affirm Allah's attributes are eternal: 'لم يزل بصفاته أولاً قديراً ولا يزال عالماً خبيراً'. Also note the descriptions of His knowledge, will, and power.
These affirm that Allah has always been powerful and will always be knowing.
4
Understand the outcome of these attributes
Read the final part: 'خلق الأشياء بقدرته... فذل لعظمته المتكبرون'. How does this conclude the doxology?
It shows that creation is humbled before Allah's greatness.

The Created Qur'an and the Polytheists' Claim
Al-Ash'ari equates Mu'tazila doctrine with polytheist rejection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Ash'ari considered the doctrine of the created Qur'an to be equivalent to the polytheists' rejection of divine revelation.

Core Idea
Believing the Qur'an is created equates it to human speech – the same claim as the polytheists.

In this brief but powerful passage, al-Ash'ari draws a direct parallel between the Mu'tazila position on the Qur'an and the statement of the polytheists who dismissed the Qur'an as mere human speech. He is not merely stating a doctrinal difference; he is issuing a theological condemnation, implying that the Mu'tazila have aligned themselves with the enemies of revelation. This lesson unpacks that accusation and its implications for understanding the uncreatedness of the Qur'an.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the two groups mentioned: the Mu'tazila (implied by 'they') and the polytheists (al-mushrikin).
The verse citation is Qur'an 74:25, where the polytheists say: 'This is nothing but the speech of a human being.'
2
Identify the comparison being made
Al-Ash'ari says the Mu'tazila adopted the createdness of the Qur'an 'analogous to' (naziran li) the polytheists' statement. What is the exact claim he attributes to both groups?
Both groups reduce the Qur'an to human speech – the polytheists explicitly, the Mu'tazila by claiming it is created.
3
Reflect on the rhetorical strategy
Ask yourself: Why does al-Ash'ari choose to frame the Mu'tazila position in this way? What does this tell you about the seriousness of the issue in his view?
This is not a neutral theological disagreement; it is an accusation of heresy by association.
4
Consider the broader implication
If the Qur'an is created, it is contingent and thus not eternal divine speech. Al-Ash'ari's point is that such a view undermines the divine origin of revelation itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودانوا بخلق القرآن نظيراً لقول إخوانهم من المشركين الذين قالوا: { إِنْ هَذَا إِلَّا قَوْلُ الْبَشَرِ } فزعموا أن القرآن كقول البشر.
And they adopted the createdness of the Qur'an, analogous to the statement of their brethren from the polytheists who said: 'This is nothing but the speech of a human being' (Qur'an 74:25). So they claimed that the Qur'an is like human speech.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
In this accusation, al-Ash'ari links the Mu'tazila doctrine of the created Qur’an to the polytheists. He cites the Qur'anic verse in which the polytheists dismiss the Qur’an as merely human speech. By claiming that the Qur’an is created, the Mu'tazila are effectively equating it with human speech, thus aligning themselves with the polytheists. This is a strong theological condemnation.

Key Terms
خلق القرآن
قول البشر
المشركون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the debate over the createdness of the Qur'an is a minor theological technicality.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari shows it is a fundamental issue: if the Qur'an is created, it is like human speech, which undermines its status as divine revelation.

Checkpoint
Whose statement does al-Ash'ari compare the belief in a created Qur'an to?
A) The Jews
B) The Christians
C) The polytheists (mushrikin)
D) The philosophers

Key Takeaway
To call the Qur'an created is, for al-Ash'ari, to place oneself in the company of those who rejected it as mere human speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself treating the Qur'an as just a book of guidance rather than the very speech of Allah? Where in your daily life do you fail to honor it as uncreated and divine? What one practice can you start today to change that?
?
When you read this passage, do you sense the weight of al-Ash'ari's accusation? In what ways might you be aligning yourself with those who dismiss the Qur'an as merely human—by neglecting its study, prioritizing your own thoughts over its commands, or feeling apathetic towards its recitation?
?
The polytheists said, 'This is nothing but human speech.' If you honestly examine your heart, do you ever share that same indifference? What would it mean for you to truly believe that every verse is the eternal speech of Allah? How would that change your next interaction with the Qur'an?

Refuting the Qadariyyah: The Absolute Efficacy of God's Will
Refutation of Qadariyyah belief in ineffective divine will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Qadariyyah belief that God's will can be thwarted contradicts the Quranic consensus and constitutes a dualistic heresy.

Core Idea
God's will always prevails; nothing happens without His will.

This passage from Imam al-Ash'ari refutes the Qadariyyah who claimed that God wills what does not happen and what happens He does not will. Imam al-Ash'ari demonstrates that this contradicts the consensus of Muslims and numerous Quranic verses that affirm the absolute effectiveness of God's will. He also reveals why the Prophet called them the 'Majus of this nation', linking their belief to dualistic tendencies.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp the argument without interpretation.
Pay attention to the tone of refutation.
2
Identify the core claim and refutation
Notice the Qadariyyah's claim: God wills what does not happen and what happens He does not will. Then see how the author counters with consensus and Quranic verses.
The five verses are key evidence.
3
Reflect on the Majus comparison
Understand why the Prophet likened them to the Majus. This reveals the theological error of attributing events to a source other than God's will.
This comparison underscores the seriousness of the deviation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعموا أن الله عز وجل يشاء ما لا يكون ويكون مالا يشاء، خلافاً لما أجمع عليه المسلمون من أن ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن، ورداً لقول الله عز وجل: ﴿وَمَا تَشَاءُونَ إِلَّا أَن يَشَاءَ اللهُ﴾ [الإنسان: ٣٠]. فأخبر تعالى أنا لا نشاء شيئاً إلا وقد شاء الله أن نشاءه، ولقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَوْ شَاءَ اللهُ مَا أَقْتَتَلُوا﴾ [البقرة: ٢٥٣]، ولقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَاَنَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هدتها﴾ [السجدة: ١٣]، ولقوله تعالى: ﴿فَعَّالٌ لِّمَا يُرِيدُ﴾ [البروج: ١٦]، ولقوله تعالى مخبراً عن نبيه شعيب أنه قال: ﴿وَمَا يَكُونُ لَنَا أَن نَّعُودَ فِيهَا إِلَّا أَن يَشَاءَ اللَّهُ رَبُّنَا﴾ [الأعراف: ٨٩]. ولهذا سماهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مجوس هذه الأمة؛ لأنهم دانوا بديانة المجوس وضاهوا أقاويلهم.
And they claimed that God Almighty wills what does not happen and what happens He does not will, contrary to the consensus of the Muslims that what God wills happens and what He does not will does not happen, and in opposition to the saying of God Almighty: 'And you do not will except that God wills' [Surah al-Insan:30]. So He informed us that we do not will anything unless God wills that we will it; and to His saying: 'And if God had willed, they would not have fought' [Surah al-Baqarah:253]; and to His saying: 'And if We had willed, We could have given every soul its guidance' [Surah al-Sajdah:13]; and to His saying: 'Doer of whatever He wills' [Surah al-Buruj:16]; and to His saying, informing about His prophet Shu'ayb that he said: 'And it is not for us to return to it unless God, our Lord, wills' [Surah al-A'raf:89]. And for this, the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, called them the Majus of this nation, because they adhered to the religion of the Majus and emulated their sayings.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyyah's belief that God's will can be ineffective. The author states that this contradicts the consensus of Muslims and numerous Quranic verses affirming the absolute efficacy of God's will. He then explains why the Prophet called them the 'Majus of this nation' for adopting dualistic ideas.

Key Terms
المشيئة
الإجماع
مجوس هذه الأمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God wills what does not happen and what happens He does not will.
Correction: God's will is always effective; what He wills happens and what He does not will does not happen.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say the Prophet called the Qadariyyah 'Majus of this nation'?
A) Because they worship fire
B) Because they adopted the dualistic belief of the Majus
C) Because they deny fate
D) Because they rejected scripture

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyyah belief that evil occurs without God's will is a dualistic heresy condemned by the Quran and the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as if there is a domain of your life that is outside God's will, a place where you believe you have the final say? How does that contradict what this passage teaches about God's absolute will, and what would it look like to surrender that domain to Him today?
?
When you reflect on your past sins, do you acknowledge that they occurred under God's will yet you bear responsibility, or do you secretly believe that God's will was not involved? How does the Qadariyyah error manifest in your heart, and what verse from this passage can you use to correct it?
?
The Prophet called the Qadariyyah the 'Majus of this nation' because of their dualistic thinking. In what subtle ways do you still divide your life into what is 'God's part' and what is 'your part'? What is one concrete area you will consciously remind yourself that 'nothing happens without God's will'?

Learning Objective

No one owns harm or benefit except Allah.

In this passage, Imam al-Ash'ari refutes this notion by citing a verse where even the Prophet is commanded to disavow such power. Let's examine the proof.

This connects to the core idea of tawhid.

Denial of Divine Attributes: Face, Hands, Eyes
Al-Ash'ari enumerates three attributes denied by a sect and refutes each with a verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ash'ari defends the attributes of Face, Hands, and Eyes by citing Quranic verses against those who deny them.

Core Idea
Affirming Allah's attributes through Quranic texts without interpretation.

This lesson presents Al-Ash'ari's refutation of a sect that denies three specific divine attributes: face, hands, and eyes. By citing explicit Quranic verses, he affirms these attributes as they are mentioned. The lesson highlights the importance of accepting divine descriptions without metaphorical reinterpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three denied attributes
Read the Arabic passage once and identify which three attributes are being denied. Notice how each denial is followed by a Quranic verse.
2
For each attribute, note the Quranic verse cited
Write down the verse reference for each attribute: face (Ar-Rahman 27), hands (Sad 75), eyes (Al-Qamar 14 and Taha 39).
These are direct citations from the Quran.
3
Reflect on the method of refutation
Observe that Al-Ash'ari does not use rational arguments here but simply cites the Quran. Consider why this is a strong refutation for the sect.
The sect likely relied on rational interpretations; Al-Ash'ari counters with revelation.
4
Consider the principle of affirming attributes without modality
Think about why affirming these attributes does not mean comparing Allah to creation. The commentary explains this is tafwid (consigning the meaning to Allah).
This avoids anthropomorphism while accepting the text literally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودفعوا أن يكون الله وجه مع قوله عز وجل: {وَيَبْقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو الْجَلَالِ وَالْإِكْرَامِ} [الرحمن: 27]. وأنكروا أن له يدان مع قوله سبحانه: {لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَيَّ} [ص: 75]. وأنكروا أن يكون له عين مع قوله سبحانه: {تَجْرِي بِأَعْيُنِنَا} [القمر: 14]، وقوله: {وَلِتُصْنَعَ عَلَى عَيْنِي} [طه: 39].
And they repudiated that Allah has a face, along with His saying, Mighty and Majestic: {And there will remain the Face of your Lord, Possessor of Majesty and Honor} [ar-Rahman: 27]. And they denied that He has hands, along with His saying, Exalted is He: {For what I created with My hands} [Sad: 75]. And they denied that He has an eye, along with His saying, Exalted is He: {Sailing under Our eyes} [al-Qamar: 14], and His saying: {And that you be formed under My eye} [Taha: 39].
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
These are three consecutive accusations (16-18) against the heretical sect: they deny that Allah has a face, hands, and eyes. Al-Ash'ari refutes each by citing explicit Qur'anic verses. For the face, he quotes Surah ar-Rahman 27, which speaks of the 'Face of your Lord' remaining. For hands, Surah Sad 75, where Allah says He created Adam with 'My two hands.' For eyes, Surah al-Qamar 14 and Taha 39 refer to the ark sailing 'under Our eyes' and Moses being formed 'under My eye.' The sect interprets these verses metaphorically (ta'wil), but al-Ash'ari insists on affirming the attributes as they are mentioned in the Qur'an without modality (tafwid).

أنكروا

Correction: Al-Ash'ari and the Salaf affirm these attributes without modality or comparison, as they are mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway

Al-Ash'ari lists denial of divine knowledge and power with Qur'anic refutations.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Denying Allah's knowledge and power contradicts clear Qur'anic affirmations.

Al-Ash'ari continues to list heresies, now turning to the denial of two fundamental divine attributes: knowledge and power. He counters each denial with a direct Qur'anic verse that explicitly attributes these qualities to Allah. This lesson will examine these two refutations and their scriptural basis.

This affirms power as a real attribute.

In this final accusation, Al-Ash'ari concludes his list of heresies by pointing out that the sect rejects well-known hadith about Allah's descent. This denial reflects their broader approach of interpreting away divine attributes. Al-Ash'ari affirms the hadith as narrated, without modality.

Six Attributes Denied by Deviant Sects
Al-Ash'ari lists six attributes denied by deviant sects with scriptural proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six attributes that deviant sects deny from God and the scriptural proofs al-Ash'ari uses to affirm them.

Core Idea
Affirming God's attributes is rooted in scripture, not speculation.

In this passage, Imam al-Ash'ari documents a pattern of deviance: certain sects deny specific divine attributes despite clear scriptural evidence. He lists six attributes—face, hands, eye, knowledge, power, and descent—each with a Quranic verse or hadith as proof. This lesson walks through each denial and its refutation, showing how al-Ash'ari anchors theology in revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the translation. Notice the pattern: each denial is followed by a scripture quote.
The passage uses the same structure for each attribute.
2
Identify the six attributes
List each attribute that the deviant sects deny. Check them against the scriptural proofs al-Ash'ari provides.
The attributes are: face, hands, eye, knowledge, power, and descent.
3
Understand the refutation method
For each denial, al-Ash'ari cites a clear Quranic verse or hadith. This shows that the attributes are affirmed in revelation, not invented.
This counters the sects' rationalist denial.
4
Address the common misunderstanding
Deviant sects claimed affirming these attributes implies anthropomorphism (tashbih). Al-Ash'ari affirms them without modality or likeness.
The passage itself does not discuss tashbih, but it is the underlying issue.
5
Reflect on the importance of scripture
Consider why al-Ash'ari prioritizes scriptural evidence over rational arguments for these attributes.
This reflects the Sunni methodology of giving precedence to revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
-١٦ ودفعوا أن يكون الله وجه مع قوله عز وجل: ﴿وَيَبْقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو الجَالِ وَالْإِكْرَامِ ﴾ [الرحمن: ۲۷] . -۱۷ وأنكروا أن له يدان مع قوله سبحانه: ﴿ لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَيَّ ) [ ص: ٧٥] . -۱۸ وأنكروا أن يكون له عين مع قوله سبحانه : ( تجرى بِأَعْيُنِنَا ) [القمر: ١٤] ، وقوله : ( وَلِتُصْنَعَ عَلَى عَيْنِ ) [ طه : ٣٩]. -۱۹ وأنكروا أن يكون الله علم مع قوله: ﴿ أَنزَلَهُ بِعِلمِهِ) [النساء : ١٦٦] . -۲۰ وأنكروا أن تكون الله قوة مع قوله سبحانه: ﴿ ذُو الْقُوَّةِ الْمَتِينُ ) [الذاريات : ٥٨ ] . -۲۱ ونفوا ما رُوي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : « أَنَّ اللَّهَ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ يَنْزِلُ كُلَّ لَيْلَةٍ إِلَى سَمَاءِ الدُّنْيَا ...... -16 And they denied that God has a face, despite His saying, Mighty and Majestic: {And there remains the Face of your Lord, Owner of Majesty and Honor} [Ar-Rahman: 27]. -17 And they denied that He has hands, despite His saying, Glorified: {For what I created with My hands} [Sad: 75]. -18 And they denied that He has an eye, despite His saying, Glorified: {Sailing under Our eyes} [Al-Qamar: 14], and His saying: {And that you be made under My eye} [Ta-Ha: 39]. -19 And they denied that God has knowledge, despite His saying: {He sent it down with His knowledge} [An-Nisa: 166]. -20 And they denied that God has power, despite His saying, Glorified: {Possessor of Power, the Strong} [Adh-Dhariyat: 58]. -21 And they denied what was narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Indeed God, Mighty and Majestic, descends every night to the heaven of the world...' and other things narrated by reliable narrators from the Messenger of God (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of six attributes that certain deviant sects (likely the Jahmiyyah and Mu'tazilah) denied, contrasted with scriptural proofs affirming them. Al-Ash'ari lists each denial with a corresponding Quranic verse or hadith. The attributes are: Face (وجه), Hands (يدان), Eye (عين), Knowledge (علم), Power (قوة), and Descent (نزول). The author's purpose is to document their rejection as a prelude to refuting them. The passage follows the author's own order: first the denial of distinct scriptural attestations, then the denial of a well-known hadith about divine descent. The phrase 'and other things' indicates that this is not an exhaustive list.

علم

نزول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming attributes like face, hands, etc., implies God is like a human (anthropomorphism).
Correction: Al-Ash'ari affirms these attributes as stated in scripture without modality or likeness (bila kayf wa la tashbih). The attributes are real but not comparable to creation.

Affirming Allah's Face without How
Imam al-Ash'ari affirms the attribute of face with the condition of tafwid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari principle of affirming the attribute of 'face' for Allah with the qualification 'bila kayf' (without how).

Core Idea
We affirm what Allah says about Himself without asking how.

This short but powerful passage from Imam al-Ash'ari establishes a key principle in Sunni theology: we affirm the divine attributes as they appear in the Quran without attempting to explain their modality. The attribute of 'face' (wajh) is mentioned in the Quran, and we accept it as real, without comparing it to created things.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the citation from the Quran.
2
Understand 'bila kayf'
Reflect on the meaning of 'bila kayf' (without how). It is a methodological principle: we affirm the reality of the attribute but do not ask or answer 'how' it exists.
This prevents anthropomorphism and tashbih.
3
See the Quranic proof
Identify the verse cited (Surah al-Rahman, 27). Notice how the author uses it as evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٨- وأن له سبحانه وجهاً بلا كيف كما قال : ( وَبَقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو الملل والإكْرَامِ ) [الرحمن : ٢٧]
28 - And that He, glorified, has a face without how, as He said: 'And there remains the Face of your Lord, the Possessor of Majesty and Honor.'
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage affirms the attribute of wajh (face) for Allah, but with the qualification 'without how' (bila kayf). This is a key Ash'ari principle: affirm the attribute as stated in the Quran, but refrain from asking how it is, denying any likeness to creation.
