Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari methodology affirms all Quranic attributes of Allah, including 'face,' while refraining from inquiring into the 'how' of their reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about Allah's face, do you ever catch yourself trying to imagine it? What does that reveal about your heart's need to grasp the Unseen? Will you commit to stopping those thoughts and affirming 'bila kayf'?
?

?
The verse says Allah's face remains after all else perishes. Is your attachment to the temporary things of this world stronger than your longing for the eternal Face of your Lord? How will you shift your focus today?

Affirming Allah's Two Hands Without How
The author affirms Allah's attribute of two hands (yadayn) with 'bila kayf' and two Quranic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'ari school affirms Allah's two hands without modality, and how Quranic verses are used as evidence.

Core Idea
Allah's hands are real but beyond human comparison – affirmed without asking how.

This passage continues the Ash'ari method of affirming divine attributes exactly as they appear in revelation, without delving into how they are. The author cites two clear Quranic verses and adds 'bila kayf' to guard against anthropomorphism. Understanding this approach is essential for grasping the Islamic stance on divine attributes.

1
Read the passage and translation

The passage is short but packed with meaning.
2

3
Understand 'bila kayf'
The phrase 'bila kayf' (without how) is critical. It means we affirm the attribute but refrain from asking or explaining its modality. This preserves transcendence.
This is the core of the Ash'ari approach.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why the author felt it necessary to state this clearly. What wrong beliefs does this guard against?
Connects to the common misunderstanding.

Allah has an eye — but we do not ask how.

This short lesson continues the method of affirming Allah's attributes as mentioned in the Quran without delving into modality. The author, Imam al-Ash'ari, affirms the attribute of 'ayn (eye) for Allah based on a clear verse from the story of Noah. The qualification 'bila kayf' reminds us that we accept the attribute while affirming Allah's transcendence.

The addition of 'bila kayf' is crucial.

4

The verse from Surah Al-Qamar (54:14) speaks of the ark floating under Allah's eyes. Ask yourself: does this verse affirm a literal eye? The author says yes, but without modality.
This is a standard method of the early scholars.

The Name of Allah is Not Other Than Him
The author condemns as misguided anyone who claims Allah's name is other than Him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position that Allah's names are not separate from His essence, and why claiming otherwise is considered misguided.

Core Idea
Allah's name is not a separate entity; it is His essence with attributes.

This short passage from Imam al-Ash'ari addresses a critical theological point: the relationship between Allah's names and His essence. The author declares that anyone who claims Allah's name is something other than Allah himself is misguided. This teaching counters the view that names are created or distinct from the named.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic sentence and its translation. Note the concise and definitive style of the author.
The passage is a single declarative sentence.
2
Identify the key claim
The passage condemns those who claim the name is 'other than Him'. Understand what 'other than' (ghayruhu) implies in this context.
3
Learn the theological background
This is part of the Ash'ari position that divine names are not separate from the essence; they are the essence with attributes. Recognize the opposing view (e.g., Mu'tazila) that names are created.
4
Reflect on implications
Consider how this teaching affects the understanding of Allah's attributes and the unity of His essence.
This doctrine safeguards tawhid by not allowing any separation between Allah and His names.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣١- وأن من زعم أن اسم الله غيره كان ضالاً .
31 - And that whoever claims that the name of Allah is other than Him is misguided.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This brief passage addresses the issue of the divine names: whether God's names are identical to His essence or distinct. The author declares that anyone who claims that Allah's name is something other than Allah is astray. This aligns with the Ash'ari position that the names of Allah are not other than His essence; they are His essence with attributes. This is a refutation of those who separate the names from the named, such as some Mu'tazila who held that names are created.

Key Terms

غيره
ضال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this passage is about the word 'Allah' being uncreated.
Correction: The actual point is that the name of Allah is not a separate entity from Allah Himself; it is identical to His essence.

Key Takeaway
The divine name is not other than the divine essence; to say otherwise is deviance.

Affirming Allah's Face, Hands, and Eyes without How
Al-Ash'ari affirms the attributes of face, hands, and eyes for Allah without modality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Al-Ash'ari affirms the attributes of face, hands, and eyes for Allah without modality (bila kayf), basing this on Quranic verses while avoiding anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are real, but their modality is unknown.

In this passage, Imam al-Ash'ari confronts a key theological challenge: how to interpret the Quranic descriptions of Allah's face, hands, and eyes. He affirms them as genuine attributes while insisting that we cannot know the 'how' (kayf). This is the balanced path between outright denial and crude anthropomorphism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic slowly, then the English. Notice the three numbered items and the consistent phrase 'bila kayf'.
2
Identify the three attributes
Find the words for face (wajh), hands (yadayn), and eye ('ayn) in the Arabic. See how each is linked to a Quranic verse.
The verses are from Surat ar-Rahman, Sad, al-Ma'idah, and al-Qamar.
3
Understand 'bila kayf'
This phrase means 'without how' – we affirm the attribute as real but do not know its modality. Contrast this with tashbih (likening to creation) and ta'til (denial).
4
Reflect on the balanced approach
Al-Ash'ari's method upholds both divine transcendence and the literal text. Ask yourself: why is it important to neither deny nor anthropomorphize?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۸ - وأن له سبحانه وجهاً بلا كيف كما قال: ﴿ وَبَقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو الْجَلَالِ وَالْإِكْرَامِ ﴾ [الرحمن: ٢٧]. ٢٩ - وأن له سبحانه يدين بلا كيف، كما قال سبحانه: ﴿ خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَيَّ ﴾ [ص: ٧٥] وكما قال: ﴿ بَلْ يَدَاهُ مَبْسُوطَتَانِ ﴾ [المائدة: ٦٤]. ٣٠ - وأن له عيناً بلا كيف كما قال سبحانه: ﴿ تَجْرِي بِأَعْيُنِنَا ﴾ [القمر: ١٤].
28. And that He, exalted, has a face without how, as He said: 'And there remains the Face of your Lord, the Owner of Majesty and Honor' (Ar-Rahman 55:27). 29. And that He, exalted, has two hands without how, as He said: 'I created with My two hands' (Sad 38:75) and as He said: 'Nay, both His hands are outstretched' (Al-Ma'idah 5:64). 30. And that He has an eye without how, as He said: 'Sailing under Our eyes' (Al-Qamar 54:14).
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a classic articulation of the Ash'ari stance on the anthropomorphic attributes mentioned in the Quran. Al-Ash'ari affirms three attributes: wajh (face), yad (hand), and 'ayn (eye) for Allah, each qualified by the phrase 'bila kayf' (without how). He provides Quranic evidence for each: for face, he cites Surah Ar-Rahman; for hands, two verses from Surah Sad and Al-Ma'idah; for eyes, from Surah Al-Qamar. The repetition of 'bila kayf' emphasizes that these attributes are real but their modality is unknown to us, avoiding both ta'til (denial) and tashbih (likening to creation). This is the balanced approach of the Salaf and the Ash'ari school.

Key Terms
وجه
يد
عين
بلا كيف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming 'hands' for Allah means He has physical limbs like humans.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari insists on 'bila kayf' – the attribute is real but its modality is unknown and unlike creation.

Checkpoint
What is the consistent qualification Al-Ash'ari applies to the attributes of face, hands, and eyes?
A) They are metaphorical
B) They are without how (bila kayf)
C) They are to be understood as acts of power
D) They are denied outright

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari affirms the attributes of face, hands, and eyes without how, maintaining divine transcendence while upholding the literal text.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'Wa baqa wajhu rabbika' (55:27), do you feel the weight of His enduring majesty, or do you let your mind drift because you cannot picture a face without how? This week, pause at every mention of Allah's attributes in your recitation and silently say 'bila kayf' — submit your intellect to His revelation.
?
The verse 'Bal yadahu mabsutatani' (5:64) tells you that Allah's hands are outstretched. Do you live as if His giving is constant, or do you despair when your duas seem unanswered? Starting today, list one specific way His 'outstretched hands' have provided for you, and thank Him in sujood.
?
You are sailing under His eyes (54:14). Is there any corner of your life where you act as if He does not see? Commit this week to changing one secret action — whether a hidden sin or a private good deed — because you know His eye is upon you.

The Name of Allah is not other than Him

Learning Objective

Allah's name is not separate from Him; to claim otherwise is to go astray.

This brief but powerful statement from Imam Al-Ash'ari addresses a key theological dispute: Are Allah's names distinct entities or are they identical with His essence? Al-Ash'ari declares that those who separate the name from the named are misguided. This lesson unpacks that assertion and its implications.

Guided Path

Affirming Knowledge, Power, Hearing, and Sight for Allah
Al-Ash'ari affirms attributes with Quranic proofs and refutes deviant negations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah possesses the attributes of knowledge, power, hearing, and sight, and how Al-Ash'ari uses Quranic verses to affirm them while rejecting the denials of deviant sects.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are affirmed by the Qur'an, not by human analogy.

In this passage, Al-Ash'ari continues his method of affirming divine attributes based on explicit Quranic texts. He addresses four essential attributes—knowledge, power, hearing, and sight—each supported by a verse. Importantly, he contrasts his position with that of the Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, and Khawarij, who denied hearing and sight due to anthropomorphic fears. This lesson establishes the Sunni principle of affirming attributes without ta'til (negation) or tashbih (comparison).

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the three points in Arabic and English, noticing the Quranic citations.
2
Identify each attribute and its proof
For each point, note the attribute (knowledge, power, hearing/sight) and the specific verse used as evidence.
Power is supported by verse 41:15.
3
Understand the sectarian context
Reflect on why Al-Ash'ari names the Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, and Khawarij as those who negate hearing and sight.
These groups denied these attributes to avoid anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۲- وأن الله علم كما قال: ﴿ أَنزَلَهُ بِعِلْمِهِ ﴾ [النساء: ١٦٦] وكما قال: ﴿ وَمَا تَحْمِلُ مِنْ أُنثَى وَلَا تَضَعُ إِلَّا بِعِلْمِهِ ﴾ [فاطر: ١١]. ٣٣- ونثبت أن الله قوة كما قال: ﴿ أَوَلَمْ يَرَوْا أَنَّ اللَّهَ الَّذِي خَلَقَهُمْ هُوَ أَشَدُّ مِنْهُمْ قُوَّةً ﴾ [فصلت: ١٥]. ٣٤- ونثبت الله السمع والبصر، ولا ننفي ذلك، كما نَفَتْه المعتزلة والجهمية والخوارج.
32. And that Allah has knowledge, as He said: 'He sent it down with His knowledge' (An-Nisa 4:166) and as He said: 'And no female conceives nor gives birth except with His knowledge' (Fatir 35:11). 33. And we affirm that Allah has power, as He said: 'Do they not see that Allah who created them is more powerful than them?' (Fussilat 41:15). 34. And we affirm for Allah hearing and sight, and we do not negate that, as the Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, and Khawarij have negated it.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage affirms four essential attributes: knowledge (ilm), power (quwwa), hearing (sam'), and sight (basar). Each is supported by a Quranic verse. Al-Ash'ari specifically contrasts his position with that of the Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, and Khawarij, who denied these attributes (especially hearing and sight) because they considered them to imply anthropomorphism. Al-Ash'ari insists on affirmation without negation. Note that for power, he uses the word 'quwwa' which is less common than 'qudra', but it is synonymous.

Key Terms
علم
قوة
سمع
بصر
معتزلة
جهمية
خوارج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some groups think that affirming hearing and sight for Allah implies He has physical organs like humans.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari affirms these attributes without modality or comparison to creation, as the Quran does.

Checkpoint
Which groups does Al-Ash'ari accuse of negating hearing and sight from Allah?
A) Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, and Khawarij
B) Ash'aris and Maturidis
C) Shi'a and Sufis
D) Philosophers and Christians

Key Takeaway
Allah's attributes of knowledge, power, hearing, and sight are firmly established by the Qur'an, and Muslims must affirm them without denial or comparison.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Allah knows every detail of your life, as the verse says 'no female conceives nor gives birth except with His knowledge'? How does this change the way you live your daily actions?
?
The passage mentions that the Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, and Khawarij negated hearing and sight. Have you ever found yourself doubting any of Allah's attributes because you could not comprehend them? What does this lesson call you to do instead?
?
Affirming that Allah has power (quwwa) means that He is more powerful than all creation. In what areas of your life are you acting as if you are in control, forgetting that Allah's power is supreme? What step will you take today to surrender that control to Him?

The Qur'an is Uncreated
Al-Ash'ari affirms that Allah's speech is uncreated and provides scriptural evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Al-Ash'ari insists that Allah's speech (the Qur'an) is uncreated and how he grounds this claim in the Quran.

Core Idea
Allah's speech is eternal and uncreated, just like His other attributes.

This lesson tackles one of the most defining theological debates of early Islam: is the Qur'an created or uncreated? Al-Ash'ari takes a firm stand, affirming that Allah's speech is not a creation but an eternal attribute. He anchors his position in a verse where Allah's creative command 'Be' brings things into existence, showing that His speech precedes creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the literal translation. Notice the clear, creedal tone: 'And we say: Indeed, the speech of Allah is uncreated.'
2
Understand the theological context
Reflect on why this statement was controversial. The Mu'tazila argued the Qur'an was created; Al-Ash'ari asserts it is uncreated, aligning with the Sunni position.
The phrase 'and we say' indicates this is a community creed.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Al-Ash'ari quotes verse 16:40. Notice how he uses it: Allah's word 'Be' is part of His speech that brings things into existence. If His speech were created, it would need to be preceded by another speech, leading to an infinite regress.
The verse is presented as evidence for the uncreated nature of Allah's speech.
4
Distinguish between speech and recitation
A common misunderstanding is that the recited Qur'an is created. Al-Ash'ari's position is that the divine speech itself is uncreated, while our recitation and writing are human acts.
This distinction helped later theologians reconcile the eternity of the Qur'an with its being recited in time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣٥ ونقول : إن كلام الله غير مخلوق، وإنه سبحانه لم يخلق شيئاً إلا وقد قال له : كن فيكون، كما قال: ﴿ إِنَّمَا قَوْلُنَا لِشَيْءٍ إِذَا أَرَدْنَاهُ أَن نَّقُولَ لَهُ كُن فَيَكُونُ ﴾ [النحل: ٤٠].
35. And we say: Indeed, the speech of Allah is uncreated, and that He, exalted, did not create anything except that He said to it: 'Be,' and it becomes, as He said: 'Indeed, Our word to a thing when We intend it is only that We say to it, "Be," and it becomes' (An-Nahl 16:40).
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage addresses a major theological controversy of the early Islamic period: whether the Qur'an is created or uncreated. Al-Ash'ari firmly states that the speech of Allah (kalam Allah) is uncreated (ghayru makhluq). He supports this by citing the verse where Allah's creative word 'Be' brings things into existence, implying that His speech is eternal and not a created entity. This became the defining creed of Ahl al-Sunnah against the Mu'tazila who claimed the Qur'an was created.

Key Terms
كلام الله
غير مخلوق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qur'an as recited and written is created.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari holds that the divine speech itself (the attribute of Allah) is uncreated, while the human recitation (qira'ah) and the physical book (mushaf) are created acts and objects. The distinction avoids confusion.

Checkpoint
What is Al-Ash'ari's position on Allah's speech as stated in this passage?
A) It is created
B) It is uncreated
C) It is both created and uncreated
D) He remains silent

Key Takeaway
Allah's speech is an eternal, uncreated attribute, proven by the fact that His command 'Be' brings creation into existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you read the Qur'an, do you sense that you are engaging with the very words of the Creator, whose command 'Be' brings things into existence? What would change in your heart if you fully believed that?
?
If Allah's speech is uncreated and eternal, then the Qur'an is not just a historical text but a living address to you today. Are you listening with the awareness that His words are as real and powerful as the command 'Be' that created the universe?

Affirming God's Knowledge, Power, Hearing, and Sight
Ashari affirms divine attributes and refutes Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, and Khawarij.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Imam Ashari affirms divine attributes like knowledge, power, hearing, and sight based on Quranic evidence, and how he refutes the Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, and Khawarij who deny them.

Core Idea
God's attributes are real and affirmed by the Quran, against those who negate them.

Imam Ashari begins this section by affirming key divine attributes directly from the Quran. He grounds his theology in scriptural evidence, contrasting his position with the Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, and Khawarij. This lesson explores his method and the specific attributes he defends.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the literal translation. Pay attention to the structure of three affirmations.
The Arabic includes an incomplete verse for power; note the [؟] placeholder.
2
Identify the attributes and their proofs
List the four attributes: knowledge, power, hearing, sight. For each, note the Quranic verse(s) Ashari cites as evidence.
The proof for power is a partial verse that likely concludes 'more powerful than them'.
3
Understand the refutation of sects
Notice that Ashari explicitly contrasts his affirmation of hearing and sight with the Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, and Khawarij. Understand that these groups denied these attributes.
This shows Ashari's polemical context.

Finally, he affirms hearing and sight for God, explicitly contrasting his position with the Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, and Khawarij, who denied these attributes. Ashari bases each affirmation on scripture and refutes those who deviate.

The Uncreatedness of God's Speech
Ashari declares God's speech uncreated and cites the 'Be' command.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Ashari affirms God's speech as an uncreated attribute and supports it with the Quranic 'Be' command.

Core Idea
God's speech is not created; it is His eternal command.

Ashari begins by establishing a core tenet of Sunni theology: that God's speech is an eternal, uncreated attribute. He then reinforces this by quoting a Quranic verse that shows God's creative word 'Be' is itself part of His uncreated speech. This passage grounds the distinction between the Creator and creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: a theological claim followed by a Quranic proof.
2
Identify the two claims
The passage makes two interconnected claims: first, that God's speech is uncreated; second, that God's act of creation happens through that speech (the 'Be' command).
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Read verse 16:40. Ask yourself: How does this verse support the claim that God's speech is uncreated? The verse shows that God's word 'Be' is the direct cause of creation, implying it is eternal and not itself created.
4
Reflect on the doctrinal implication
Consider why this distinction matters: if God's speech were created, it would be part of the contingent order (like a creature). By declaring it uncreated, Ashari upholds God's transcendence and the eternity of His attributes.
This connects to later discussions on the Qur'an being uncreated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣٥ ونقول : إن كلام الله غير مخلوق، وإنه سبحانه لم يخلق شيئاً إلا وقد قال له : ( كن فيكون »، كما قال: ﴿ إِنَّمَا قَوْلُنَا لِشَن إِذا أَرَدْنَهُ أَن تَقُولَ لَهُ كُن فيَكُونُ ﴾ [النحل : ٤٠] (٢) .

Commentary

He then links this to God's act of creation: whenever God creates something, He commands it to exist with the word 'Be' (kun), and it comes into being. To support this, he quotes the Quranic verse from Surah al-Nahl (16:40), which states that God's only word to a thing He intends is 'Be, and it is.' This verse emphasizes that God's creative command is identical with His eternal speech.

Allah alone is the Creator and human actions are created by Him
Al-Ash'ari affirms that only Allah creates, and human actions are created by Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari doctrine that only Allah creates, and that human actions are created by Allah, supported by Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Only Allah creates; human actions are also created by Him.

This lesson presents a foundational belief of Ahl al-Sunna: that Allah alone is the Creator of all things, including human actions. Al-Ash'ari affirms this doctrine with multiple Quranic verses, establishing that no creature shares in the act of creation. Through these proofs, we see that our actions are created by Allah, yet we are accountable.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully to grasp the main claim.
2
Identify the core statement
Focus on the opening line: 'There is no creator except Allah, and human actions are created and predestined by Him.' This is the doctrinal foundation.
3
Examine each Quranic proof
Go through each of the five verses al-Ash'ari cites. For each, note how it directly or indirectly supports the doctrine that only Allah creates.
The verses are from Surah al-Saffat, Fatir, al-Nahl (two verses), and al-Tur.
4
Reflect on a common misunderstanding
The passage does not deny human agency. Consider how this doctrine aligns with human responsibility and accountability.
The common misunderstanding is addressed in the lesson.
5
Complete the checkpoint and activity
Test your understanding with the multiple-choice question and then do the activity to internalize the verses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۷- وأنه لا خالق إلا الله وأن أعمال العباد مخلوقة لله مقدورة له، كما قال سبحانه: ﴿ وَاللهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الصافات: ٩٦ ] (٢). وأن العباد لا يقدرون أن يخلقوا شيئاً وهم يخلقون، كما قال: ﴿هَلْ مِنْ خَالِقٍ غير الله ﴾ [فاطر: ٣]، وكما قال: ﴿ لَا يَخْلُقُونَ شَيْئًا وَهُمْ يُخْلَقُونَ ﴾ [النحل: ٢٠] ، وكما قال سبحانه: ﴿ أَفَمَن يَخْلُقُ كَمَن لا يَخْلُقُ ﴾ [النحل: ١٧]، وكما قال: ﴿ أَمْ خُلِقُوا مِنْ غَيْرِ شَيْءٍ أَمْ هُمُ الْخَالِقُونَ ﴾ [الطور: ٣٥] . وهذا في كتاب الله كثير (۳)
37. And that there is no creator except Allah, and that the actions of servants are created by Allah, predestined by Him, as He, glorified is He, said: "And Allah created you and what you do" [37:96]. And that the servants are not able to create anything while they are [themselves] created, as He said: "Is there any creator other than Allah?" [35:3], and as He said: "They do not create anything, while they are created" [16:20], and as He said, glorified is He: "Is He who creates like one who does not create?" [16:17], and as He said: "Were they created from nothing, or are they the creators?" [52:35]. And this is abundant in the Book of Allah.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal affirmation that only Allah is the Creator, and that human actions are created and predestined by Allah. Al-Ash'ari begins by stating the core belief: there is no creator except Allah, and the actions of His servants are created by Him and predetermined. He then provides multiple Quranic proofs. First, verse 37:96: 'And Allah created you and what you do' – this directly attributes the creation of both humans and their actions to Allah. Second, verse 35:3 asks rhetorically if there is any creator besides Allah, implying none. Third, verse 16:20 states that those called upon besides Allah cannot create anything while they themselves are created. Fourth, verse 16:17 contrasts the Creator with those who do not create, emphasizing the uniqueness of Allah's creative power. Fifth, verse 52:35 challenges the polytheists: were they created from nothing, or are they themselves the creators? – the answer is that Allah alone is the Creator. Al-Ash'ari concludes that such proofs are abundant in the Quran. The footnote markers (٢) and (٣) refer to scholarly references, but the main text stands as a clear declaration of the Ash'ari doctrine on divine creation of actions.

أعمال العباد
مقدورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That this teaching negates human free will or accountability.
Correction: The passage does not deny human agency; it affirms that the existence and power of actions come from Allah, while humans acquire the actions and are accountable.

Checkpoint

B) 37:96

Key Takeaway
Allah alone is the Creator of all things, including human actions; this is supported by multiple Quranic verses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your daily actions—your work, your worship, even your mistakes—do you truly believe that every single one is created by Allah? How does that belief affect your sense of dependence on Him?
?
If Allah alone creates both your obedience and your disobedience, where does your responsibility lie? How does this truth deepen your gratitude for the good He enables and your humility when you fall short?
?
Are there areas of your life where you act as if you are the independent creator of your success? What concrete step can you take today to acknowledge that even your ability to strive is a gift from Allah?

The Quran is the Uncreated Speech of Allah
Al-Ash'ari affirms the Quran as Allah's uncreated speech and declares takfir on its denier.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari doctrine that the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah and the serious consequence for denying this.

Core Idea
Denying that the Quran is uncreated is disbelief in the Ash'ari creed.

This lesson presents a foundational claim of Sunni orthodoxy. During the Mihna, the Mu'tazila argued that the Quran was created. Al-Ash'ari counters decisively: the Quran is Allah's speech, uncreated, and anyone who says otherwise is a disbeliever. This short statement carries immense weight in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation once to grasp the direct claim and the severity of the takfir.
2
Identify the two parts
Notice the affirmation (the Quran is Allah's uncreated speech) and the conditional ruling (whoever says created is a disbeliever).
3
Reflect on historical context
Consider that this was written during the Mihna, when the state enforced the createdness of the Quran. Al-Ash'ari's stance was a bold defense of orthodoxy.
4
Apply the learning
Ask yourself: Why is this attribute of speech so central? How does it relate to Allah's perfection?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤١ - ونقول: إن القرآن كلام الله غير مخلوق، وأن من قال بخلق القرآن فهو كافر
41. And we say: Indeed the Quran is the speech of Allah, uncreated, and that whoever says that the Quran is created is a disbeliever.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a clear doctrinal statement on the nature of the Quran. Al-Ash'ari asserts that the Quran is the speech of Allah (kalam Allah) and is not created (ghayr makhluq). He then pronounces takfir (declaration of disbelief) upon anyone who claims that the Quran is created. This was a central issue in the Mihna (inquisition) of the 9th century, where the Mu'tazila argued that the Quran was created, while the Ash'ari and Hanbali positions held that it is uncreated and eternal. The wording is emphatic: 'whoever says it is created is a disbeliever' – showing the gravity of this doctrine in early Sunni creed.

Correction: The doctrine applies to the attribute of speech in Allah's essence, not to the created physical medium.

B) They are a disbeliever
C) They are a sinner but not a disbeliever

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's statement establishes the Quran as the uncreated speech of Allah and considers denial of this as disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If denying that the Quran is uncreated can lead to disbelief, how seriously do you take your understanding of this issue? Have you ever doubted or spoken carelessly about the Quran's nature? Repent and resolve to guard your creed.

Divine Attributes: Hearts and Fingers
Al-Ash'ari affirms divine control of hearts and the finger attribute from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ash'ari affirms Allah's control over hearts and the finger attribute while explicitly rejecting modality (takyif).

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are affirmed without asking how.

In this passage, Imam Al-Ash'ari states two core Sunni beliefs about Allah's actions: that He turns hearts and that He places the heavens on a finger. Both are based on textual reports from the Prophet. The key is that they are accepted without attempting to imagine how they occur – a fundamental principle in classical Ash'ari theology to avoid anthropomorphism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the two distinct affirmations.
The Arabic is concise; the translation helps clarify the meaning.
2
Identify the two attributes
Find where Al-Ash'ari mentions Allah's control over hearts and the finger attribute. Note how each is introduced.
The first part talks about hearts being between two fingers; the second part mentions placing heavens on a finger.
3
Understand the principle of 'without how'
The phrase 'min ghayr takyif' is crucial. It means we do not ask or specify the modality. Reflect on why this preserves transcendence.
This is the Sunni approach: affirmation without modality or comparison.

This passage shows the Sunni middle path: affirming what Allah and His Messenger said, without distortion or denial.

Affirming Allah’s Descent Without Distortion
Imam Ash'ari affirms hadith of Allah's descent, rejecting deviant interpretations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the classical Sunni position is to affirm the hadith of Allah’s descent as transmitted, without falling into distortion or denial.

Core Idea
We affirm the descent narrations as they came, without asking how.

In this brief but powerful passage, Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari states the Sunni methodology for handling divine attribute narrations. He affirms all authentic reports about Allah's descent to the lowest heaven, including the words 'Is there anyone asking?' — and he explicitly distances himself from those who explain them away or reject them. This lesson shows the balanced path between literalism and figurative interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the original Arabic and translation. Notice the key terms: النزول (descent), أهل النقل (people of transmission), أهل الزيغ (people of deviation).
The passage is a single sentence but carries a clear stance.
2
Identify the two groups contrasted
The author contrasts 'people of transmission' (those who rely on authentic reports) with 'people of deviation' (those who distort or reject). Understand what each represents.
This shows the clear boundary of Sunni orthodoxy.
3
Reflect on the principle
The principle is tafwid (consigning the meaning to Allah) while affirming the wording. See how it avoids both false interpretation and denial.
The passage does not explain the 'how' of descent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونصدق جميع الروايات التي يثبتها أهل النقل من النزول إلى السماء الدنيا، وأن الرب عز وجل يقول: هل من سائل، هل من مستغفر، وسائر ما نقلوه وأثبتوه خلافاً لما قاله أهل الزيغ والتضليل.
And we affirm all the narrations that the people of transmission have established concerning the descent to the lowest heaven, and that the Lord (Almighty and Majestic) says: 'Is there anyone asking? Is there anyone seeking forgiveness?' and all the rest of what they have transmitted and established, contrary to what the people of deviation and misguidance have said.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a clear affirmation of the hadith about Allah's descent. The author declares acceptance of all narrations verified by the traditionists (أهل النقل) regarding the descent to the lowest heaven and the divine saying 'Is there anyone asking?' He extends this to all similar transmitted reports, explicitly contrasting his stance with that of the deviant groups who reject or distort such narrations.

أهل النقل

Allah's Coming on the Day of Judgment
Imam Ash'ari affirms Allah's coming on Judgment Day.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Imam Ash'ari affirms Allah's coming on the Day of Judgment as a real act, without assigning a modality or anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
Allah's coming on Judgment Day is real, but not like any created coming.

Imam Ash'ari begins by affirming the literal meaning of the Quranic verse describing Allah's coming on the Day of Judgment. He does not interpret it metaphorically nor does he assign a physical modality. This lesson explains how the Salaf upheld both the reality of divine acts and God's transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the key verb
Read the Arabic passage once, focusing on the verb 'يجيء'. Notice that it is followed by a Quranic proof without further explanation.
The verb 'يجيء' is active, indicating a real act.
2
Examine the Quranic proof
The verse from Surah al-Fajr (89:22) is quoted. Why is this verse chosen? It directly mentions the Lord's coming.
The author does not reinterpret the verse; he takes it at face value.
3
Reflect on 'without modality'
Even though the verse is taken literally, the author implies 'without how' by not detailing the manner. This preserves transcendence.
This is the principle of tafwid (consigning the modality to Allah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونقول: إن الله عز وجل يجيء يوم القيامة، كما قال سبحانه: {وجاء ربك والملك صفا صفا}، وإن الله يقرب من عباده كيف شاء بلا كيف، كما قال تعالى: {ونحن أقرب إليه من حبل الوريد}، وكما قال سبحانه: {ثم دنا فتدلى * فكان قاب قوسين أو أدنى}.
And we say: Indeed, Allah (Almighty and Majestic) comes on the Day of Resurrection, as He (glorified) said: 'And your Lord comes, and the angels, rank upon rank.' And indeed Allah draws near to His servants as He wills, without how, as He (exalted) said: 'And We are nearer to him than the jugular vein,' and as He (glorified) said: 'Then He drew near and came down, and was at a distance of two bow-lengths or nearer.'
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage affirms two key divine acts: the coming of Allah on the Day of Judgment and His nearness to His servants. The author cites Quranic verses literally: Surah al-Fajr (89:22) for the coming, Surah Qaf (50:16) for nearness, and Surah an-Najm (53:8-9) for the drawing near. Crucially, he qualifies the nearness with 'كيف شاء بلا كيف' (as He wills, without how), emphasizing that these actions are real but not subject to human modality.

Key Terms
المجيء (the coming)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Ash'aris deny the literal meaning of 'coming' and interpret it as a metaphor.
Correction: Ash'aris affirm the literal occurrence of the act but negate any modality or physical movement.

Checkpoint

B) He comes Himself.
C) He does not come.
D) He comes in a physical form.

Key Takeaway
Allah's coming on the Day of Judgment is an act we affirm by the Quran, without asking how.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Affirming Reports of Allah's Descent and Speech
Imam Ash'ari affirms transmitted reports of Allah's descent and speech

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Ash'ari insists on affirming transmitted reports about Allah's attributes without figurative interpretation, and how this differs from the position of ahl al-zaygh.

Core Idea
Affirm the revealed reports as they came, without asking 'how'.

Imam Ash'ari here states a core principle of Ahl al-Sunna: we accept and affirm all authentic narrations that describe Allah's actions and attributes. This includes famous reports like Allah's descent to the lowest heaven and His speech during the night. The lesson is not just about these specific examples, but about the entire method of dealing with divine attributes: acceptance without distortion.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic text and translation
Start by carefully reading the Arabic and the literal translation. Notice the key word 'نصدق' (we affirm) – it sets the tone of acceptance.
2
Understand the term 'tasdiq'
Tasdiq means to affirm as true. In this context, it means accepting the reports exactly as transmitted by reliable narrators, without reinterpreting them.
This is the opposite of ta'wil (figurative interpretation) practiced by some groups.
3
Identify the two examples given
The passage mentions two specific reports: (a) descent to the lowest heaven, (b) Allah saying 'Is there any asker?' etc. Recognize that these are examples of a larger body of accepted narrations.
4
Note the contrast with ahl al-zaygh
Imam Ash'ari explicitly mentions that his position is contrary to 'the people of deviation and misguidance' who reject or reinterpret such reports. This shows the sectarian context.
Ahl al-zaygh are often those who deny divine attributes or explain them away.
5
Reflect on the principle of 'bila kayf'
Though not explicitly in this passage, the Ash'ari approach is to affirm these reports 'without how' (bila kayf), meaning we do not attribute a modality to Allah's actions.
This safeguards tanzih (transcendence) while upholding the reports.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونصدق جميع الروايات التي يثبتها أهل النقل من النزول إلى السماء الدنيا، وأن الرب عز وجل يقول: هل من سائل، هل من مستغفر، وسائر ما نقلوه وأثبتوه خلافاً لما قاله أهل الزيغ والتضليل.
And we affirm all the narrations which the people of transmission (ahl al-naql) establish: the descent to the lowest heaven, and that the Lord, Mighty and Majestic, says: 'Is there any asker? Is there any seeker of forgiveness?', and the rest of what they narrated and established, contrary to what the people of deviation and misguidance said.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal affirmation of certain transmitted reports that describe Allah's attributes and actions. Imam Ash'ari declares that the Sunni creed is to affirm (tasdiq) all the narrations that the people of transmission (ahl al-naql, i.e., the scholars of hadith) have established. He mentions two specific examples: (1) the descent (nuzul) of Allah to the lowest heaven, a well-known hadith, and (2) that Allah says 'Is there any asker? Is there any seeker of forgiveness?' during the last third of the night. These are affirmed without ta'wil (figurative interpretation), unlike the position of the people of deviation (ahl al-zaygh) and misguidance (al-tadlil), who reject or reinterpret such reports.

Key Terms
تصديق
أهل النقل
النزول إلى السماء الدنيا
أهل الزيغ والتضليل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That affirming Allah's descent implies He moves or occupies space like created beings.
Correction: Imam Ash'ari and Ahl al-Sunna affirm the descent without how (bila kayf), maintaining that Allah is not subject to spatial or temporal limitations. The descent is a real attribute of action, but its modality is unknown.

Checkpoint
What is the basis for affirming the descent according to Imam Ash'ari?
A) Rational deduction.
B) Reports established by the people of transmission.
C) Consensus of the community.
D) Personal opinion.

Key Takeaway
Imam Ash'ari teaches that we must affirm all authentic hadith reports about Allah's attributes exactly as transmitted, without reinterpretation, while rejecting the views of those who deny them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite or hear the hadith of Allah's descent, do you feel a tension in your heart between accepting it literally and wanting to explain it away? What does that tension reveal about your trust in Allah's revelation versus your own intellect? Tonight, before sleep, meditate on that hadith and say: 'I affirm it as it came, without how.'
?
Do you ever catch yourself mentally qualifying Allah's attributes—thinking, 'this must mean something else'—to make them more comfortable for your mind? That impulse is the seed of deviation. Repent from it and commit to repeating Imam Ash'ari's phrase: 'We affirm all the narrations.'
?
Imam Ash'ari contrasts 'we affirm' with 'what the people of deviation said.' Are you more concerned with what scholars or friends might think if you affirm these reports without explanation? Whose approval do you fear more—theirs or Allah's? Make a firm intention to stand with the people of transmission, even if you stand alone.

Allah's Coming and Nearness Without Modality
Imam Ash'ari affirms Allah's coming and nearness without modality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ash'ari affirms the Quranic descriptions of Allah's coming and nearness on the Day of Resurrection while negating any modality (kayfiyya).

Core Idea
Allah's coming and nearness are real, not metaphorical — but without any how.

Imam Ash'ari begins a crucial section on the divine attributes by addressing two verses that describe Allah's actions on the Day of Resurrection and His closeness to His servants. He affirms these descriptions literally, but immediately adds the condition 'without how' to guard against any anthropomorphic interpretation. This passage demonstrates the classical Salafi-Ash'ari approach to the ambiguous verses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and the translation. Notice the three Quranic verses cited.
2
Identify the two affirmations
The passage makes two distinct claims: Allah's coming on Judgment Day, and Allah's nearness to His servants. Note the verses for each.
3
Understand the condition 'bila kayf'
Every affirmation is followed by the phrase 'as He wills, without how'. This is the key to the Ash'ari position.
4
Reflect on the significance
Why does the author insist on 'without how'? What is he protecting?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونقول: إن الله عز وجل يجيء يوم القيامة، كما قال سبحانه: {وجاء ربك والملك صفاً صفاً} وإن الله يقرب من عباده كيف شاء بلا كيف كما قال تعالى: {ونحن أقرب إليه من حبل الوريد}، وكما قال سبحانه: {ثم دنا فتدلى * فكان قاب قوسين أو أدنى}.
And we say: Indeed Allah, Mighty and Majestic, comes on the Day of Resurrection, as He said, exalted: 'And your Lord comes, and the angels in rows upon rows' (Quran 89:22). And indeed Allah draws near to His servants as He wills, without 'how' (bila kayf), as He said, exalted: 'And We are nearer to him than the jugular vein' (Quran 50:16), and as He said, exalted: 'Then He drew near and descended, and was at a distance of two bow-lengths or nearer' (Quran 53:8-9).
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage affirms two divine actions from the Quran: Allah's coming (maji') on the Day of Resurrection and His nearness (qurb) to His servants. Imam Ash'ari cites three verses: (1) 'And your Lord comes...' (al-Fajr:22), which is understood literally but without modality; (2) 'And We are nearer to him than the jugular vein' (Qaf:16), which indicates Allah's closeness to every person; and (3) 'Then He drew near and descended...' (al-Najm:8-9), which originally refers to the Prophet's ascent but Imam Ash'ari applies to Allah's nearness to His servants. He explicitly adds 'as He wills, without how' (kayfa sha'a bila kayf), which is the hallmark of the Salafi/Ash'ari position of affirming the attribute while negating any modality or anthropomorphism.

Key Terms
مجيء
قرب
بلا كيف
صفاً صفاً
قاب قوسين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some accuse Ash'aris of denying these verses by interpreting them metaphorically.
Correction: Imam Ash'ari affirms them literally but without modality, avoiding both denial and anthropomorphism.

Checkpoint
How does Imam Ash'ari describe Allah's nearness to His servants?
A) As a spatial closeness.
B) As He wills, without 'how'.
C) Only metaphorically.
D) Through His knowledge alone.

Key Takeaway
Imam Ash'ari affirms Allah's coming and nearness literally from the Quran, while insisting they are without modality (bila kayf) to preserve divine transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read 'Your Lord comes,' do you instinctively picture a movement or arrival? How does the phrase 'without how' challenge that instinct? Are you willing to affirm the reality of Allah's coming without reducing it to a mental image?
?
You claim to believe that Allah is near to you, closer than your jugular vein. But do you live as if He is that near? What would change in your life today if you truly felt His nearness in every moment, without needing to picture it?
?
The Ash'ari position requires you to affirm both the literal meaning of the verses and the negation of modality. Is your heart comfortable with that tension, or do you feel a urge to resolve it by either negating the attribute or imagining a form? How can you train your mind to accept divine attributes as realities without pictures?

On Allah's Knowledge of All Things
Affirmation that Allah knows all actions, past, present, future, and hypotheticals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's knowledge encompasses all actions, past, present, future, and even hypothetical scenarios, according to Ahl al-Sunnah.

Core Idea
Allah knows everything, even what never happens.

This article from Imam al-Ash'ari's Al-Ibanah affirms the comprehensive nature of divine omniscience. It lists several categories of things Allah knows, including the actions of servants, the past, future, and even counterfactual conditionals. This establishes that Allah's knowledge is complete and eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic original and its translation, noticing the sequence of clauses. This is a single sentence but packed with meaning.
2
Identify the categories of knowledge
List the different things Allah knows: present actions, future end, past, future, non-existent, and hypotheticals.
Each phrase expands the scope.
3
Reflect on the inclusion of hypotheticals
Consider why the author explicitly mentions 'if it were, how it would be' – this defends against any limitation on Allah's knowledge.
This counters the view that Allah doesn't know what never happens.
4
Connect to divine attribute of omniscience
Understand that this article affirms the attribute of knowledge as eternal and all-encompassing.
This is a key point in Sunni creed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٦٩ - وندين الله عز وجل بأنه يعلم ما العباد عاملون، وإلى ما هم صائرون، وما كان وما يكون وما لا يكون، وأن لو كان كيف كان يكون.
69 - And we owe duty to Allah, may He be mighty and majestic, that He knows what the servants are doing, and what they are becoming, and what was, and what will be, and what will not be, and that if it were, how it would be.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This article provides a comprehensive statement of divine omniscience. Allah knows the present actions of servants, their future states, the past, the future, what will not happen, and even counterfactual conditionals ('if it were, how it would be'). This affirms that Allah's knowledge is complete and eternal, including all possibilities.

Key Terms
علم الله
ما كان وما يكون
لو كان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah does not know hypothetical scenarios or things that never happen.
Correction: This article explicitly states that Allah knows 'what will not be' and 'if it were, how it would be', affirming His knowledge of all possibilities.

Checkpoint
What does Allah know according to this article?
A) Only the past
B) Only present
C) Everything including hypotheticals
D) Only major events

Key Takeaway
Allah's knowledge is absolute and includes all actual and possible events.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Allah knows every thought you've ever had and every thought you could have had. If you truly believed that He sees your innermost intentions, would you still entertain the same idle fantasies and hidden resentments?
?
You claim to trust in Allah's perfect plan, yet you often dwell on 'what if' scenarios and regrets. Since He already knows how the unrealized paths would have played out, can you release your attachment to those possibilities and submit fully to His decree?
?
If Allah's knowledge includes the evil you could have done but never did, does that humble you or make you proud? How does knowing that He sees the potential sin you avoided change the way you thank Him for His guidance?

Divine Knowledge and Obedience in Ash'ari's Creed
Ash'ari affirms God's exhaustive knowledge and commands obedience and separation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ash'ari's affirmation of God's comprehensive knowledge (covering past, present, future, and hypotheticals) and the dua of obedience to imams and avoidance of innovators.

Core Idea
God's knowledge encompasses all possibilities; obedience to leaders is part of sound creed.

Imam al-Ash'ari opens his creed with a powerful statement about Allah's knowledge that covers everything—past, present, future, and even hypotheticals. He then outlines two key communal duties: obedience to imams and separation from innovators. This lesson unpacks these foundational points that establish the framework for the rest of the creed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall meaning. Notice the rhythm and the assertiveness of the language.
The passage is a direct declaration of belief ('We affirm...').
2
Identify the scope of divine knowledge
Look at the first sentence. It affirms that Allah knows what servants are doing, their ultimate destiny, past, present, future, and even hypothetical events ('if it were, how it would be'). List each item affirmed.
3
Understand the practical commands
After the knowledge statement, Ash'ari includes two practical aspects: obedience to imams and sincerity to Muslims, and separation from innovators and people of desires. Note why these are part of the creed.
These are not merely ethical but doctrinal positions.
4
Reflect on the structure
Consider why Ash'ari begins with divine knowledge and then moves to communal duties. How do these two parts relate? The commentary suggests that these are foundational pillars for the rest of the arguments.
This passage sets the stage for the rest of the book.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وندين الله عز وجل بأنه يعلم ما العباد عاملون، وإلى ما هم صائرون، وما كان وما يكون وما لا يكون، وأن لو كان كيف كان يكون (١). وبطاعة الأئمة ونصيحة المسلمين . ونرى مفارقة كل داعية إلى بدعة، ومجانبة أهل الأهواء وسنحتج لما ذكرناه من قولنا وما بقي منه مما لم نذكره باباً باباً،

مقتضى صنيع مالك، وليس عنده في هذه المسألة شيء منصوص، إلا أن أصحابه صرحوا بأن أطفال المسلمين في الجنة وأطفال الكفار خاصة في المشيئة، والحجة فيه حديث : ( الله أعلم بما كانوا عاملين ) . ثانيها: أنهم تبع لآبائهم، فأولاد المسلمين في الجنة وأولاد الكفار في النار، وحكاه ابن حزم عن الأزارقة من الخوارج، واحتجوا بقوله تعالى: (رَبِّ لَا تَذَرْ عَلَى الْأَرْضِ مِنَ الْكَافِرِينَ دَيَّارًا ) وتعقبه بأن المراد قوم نوح خاصة، وإنما دعا بذلك لما أوحى الله إليه : ( أَنَّهُ لَن يُؤْمِنَ مِن قَوْمِكَ إِلَّا مَن قَدْ آمَنَ ) وأما حديث ( هم من آبائهم أو منهم ) فذاك ورد في حكم الحربي، وروى أحمد من حديث عائشة : سألت رسول الله عن ولدان المسلمين ، قال : ( في الجنة ). وعن أولاد المشركين قال : ( في النار )، فقلت : يا رسول الله لم يدركوا الأعمال ، قال : ( ربك أعلم بما كانوا عاملين، لو شئت أسمعتك تضاغيهم في النار ) وهو حديث ضعيف جداً لأن في إسناده أبا عقيل مولى بهية وهو متروك. ثالثها: أنهم يكونون في برزخ بين الجنة والنار، لأنهم لم يعملوا حسنات يدخلون بها الجنة، ولا سيئات يدخلون بها النار. رابعها: خدم أهل الجنة، وفيه حديث عن أنس ضعيف أخرجه أبو داود الطيالسي وأبو يعلى، وللطبراني والبزار من حديث سمرة مرفوعا : أولاد المشركين خدم أهل الجنة، وإسناده ضعيف. خامسها : أنهم يصيرون تراباً، روي عن ثمامة بن أشرس. سادسها : هم في النار حكاه عياض عن أحمد، وغلطه ابن تيمية بأنه قول لبعض أصحابه ولا يحفظ عن الإمام أصلاً. سابعها : أنهم يمتحنون في الآخرة بأن ترفع لهم النار، فمن دخلها كانت عليه برداً وسلاماً، ومن أبى عذب، أخرجه البزار من حديث أنس وأبي سعيد وأخرجه الطبراني من حديث معاذ بن جبل، وقد صحت مسألة الامتحان في حق المجنون، ومن مات في الفترة من طرق صحيحة، وحكى البيهقي في كتاب الاعتقاد أنه المذهب الصحيح .

وشيئاً شيئاً إن شاء الله تعالى.
And we affirm to Allah Almighty that He knows what the servants are doing, and to what they are going, and what was and what will be and what will not be, and that if it were how it would be. And (we affirm) obedience to the imams and sincerity to the Muslims. And we hold separation from every caller to innovation, and avoidance of the people of desires, and we will argue for what we have mentioned of our statement and what remains of it that we have not mentioned, section by section and point by point, if Allah wills.

The implication of Malik's practice: he has nothing explicit on this issue, but his companions stated that the children of Muslims are in Paradise and the children of disbelievers specifically are subject to the will (of Allah), and the proof is the hadith: 'Allah knows best what they were doing.' Second: they follow their fathers; the children of Muslims are in Paradise and the children of disbelievers are in Hell. Ibn Hazm reported it from the Azariqa of the Khawarij, and they argued with His saying: 'Lord, do not leave upon the earth any of the disbelievers a single inhabitant.' He refuted it by saying that the intended are the people of Noah specifically, and he only prayed that when Allah inspired him: 'None of your people will believe except those who have already believed.' As for the hadith 'They are from their fathers or from them', that is concerning the ruling of a combatant. Ahmad narrated from the hadith of Aisha: I asked the Messenger of Allah about the children of Muslims; he said: 'In Paradise.' And about the children of polytheists, he said: 'In Hell.' I said: O Messenger of Allah, they have not performed deeds; he said: 'Your Lord knows best what they were doing; if I wished I would let you hear their cries in Hell.' And it is a very weak hadith because in its chain is Abu Aqil, the freed slave of Bahiyya, who is abandoned. Third: they will be in a barrier between Paradise and Hell, because they did not do good deeds by which they enter Paradise, nor evil deeds by which they enter Hell. Fourth: servants of the people of Paradise; there is a weak hadith on it from Anas narrated by Abu Dawud al-Tayalisi and Abu Ya'la, and from Samura in the collections of al-Tabarani and al-Bazzar as marfu': 'The children of the polytheists are servants of the people of Paradise,' and its chain is weak. Fifth: they become dust; narrated from Thumama ibn Ashras. Sixth: they are in Hell; 'Iyad reported it from Ahmad, but Ibn Taymiyya corrected him saying it is a statement of some of his companions and is not preserved from the Imam at all. Seventh: they will be tested in the Hereafter: fire will be raised for them; whoever enters it will find it cool and safe, and whoever refuses will be punished. Al-Bazzar narrated it from Anas and Abu Sa'id, and al-Tabarani from Mu'adh ibn Jabal. The issue of testing has been authentically established for the insane and those who died in the interval (fatrah) through authentic chains. Al-Bayhaqi in his book 'al-I'tiqad' stated that it is the correct position.

And point by point, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage combines a creedal statement by Imam al-Ash'ari with a detailed commentary on the fate of children of polytheists. The first part is Ash'ari's creed: he affirms God's exhaustive knowledge of all past, present, future, and hypothetical events; commands obedience to rulers and sincere counsel to Muslims; and mandates separation from innovators and people of desires, promising to provide evidence section by section. The second part is a later commentary that discusses seven different opinions on the fate of children of polytheists: (1) they are subject to God's will, based on the hadith 'Allah knows best what they were doing'; (2) they follow their fathers (Muslim children in Paradise, polytheist children in Hell), attributed to the Azariqa Khawarij; (3) they remain in a barrier between Paradise and Hell; (4) they become servants of the people of Paradise; (5) they become dust; (6) they are in Hell, but Ibn Taymiyya disputes this attribution to Ahmad; (7) they are tested on the Day of Judgment by a fire, which becomes cool for those who obey and punishment for those who refuse—this opinion is endorsed by al-Bayhaqi as the correct one based on authentic traditions. The passage concludes by stating that the author will continue his explanation point by point, in sha' Allah.

Key Terms
علم الله
طاعة الأئمة
نصيحة المسلمين
بدعة
أهل الأهواء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Ash'ari affirm about Allah's knowledge regarding hypothetical events?
A) He knows them only if they happen.
B) He knows them even if they never occur.
C) He does not know them because they are unreal.
D) He knows them only in a general sense.

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari's creed begins with an all-encompassing affirmation of divine knowledge and extends to communal duties of obedience and separation from innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What does it mean for you personally that Allah knows every possibility, even the ones that never happen? How does that change how you view your past mistakes, missed opportunities, or secret thoughts that no one else knows? Will you begin to live with the awareness that nothing escapes His knowledge?
?
Ash'ari includes obedience to imams as part of creed. Which leaders or authorities are you currently obeying in your life? Are they people who uphold the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah, or do they call to innovation? If you are obeying anyone who contradicts this creed, what is holding you back from correcting your allegiance?
?
Ash'ari commands separation from innovators and people of desires. Who are the people in your life that might fall into this category? Are there friendships or attachments that you have been unwilling to distance yourself from because of comfort or fear? What step will you take today to purify your circle for the sake of your creed?

Seven Opinions on the Fate of Children of Polytheists
Commentary enumerates seven opinions on children of polytheists and endorses testing view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seven scholarly opinions on the afterlife fate of children of polytheists and the preferred view that they will be tested.

Core Idea
The fate of children of polytheists is a matter of divine will, with the strongest opinion being an afterlife test.

The commentary presents seven different views on where children of polytheists go in the afterlife, ranging from being in Heaven or Hell to becoming dust or servants. Each opinion is cited with its proof and often a critique of its authenticity. The discussion concludes by endorsing the view that they will be tested on the Day of Judgment, a position held by al-Bayhaqi.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the entire passage about the seven opinions. Note the structure: each opinion is numbered (implicitly) and accompanied by a source or argument.
The passage is dense; read carefully.
2
Identify each opinion
List all seven opinions: (1) subject to God's will, (2) follow their fathers, (3) barrier between Heaven and Hell, (4) servants of Paradise, (5) become dust, (6) in Hell, (7) tested by fire. Note the scholars or hadith associated with each.
3
Analyze the strengths and weaknesses
For each opinion, note the argument and the commentary's assessment of its strength (e.g., weak hadith, disagreement on attribution). Pay special attention to the seventh opinion which is endorsed as the correct position.
The commentary is not neutral; it leads to a conclusion.
4
Understand the endorsed view
Focus on the seventh opinion: the testing in the afterlife. Why is it considered the correct view? What evidence supports it? The commentary mentions authentic traditions for the insane and those who died in the interval (fatrah).
This view is qouted from al-Bayhaqi.

Source Text

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you believe that Allah's justice is perfect, why do you sometimes find yourself feeling uneasy or doubtful about the fate of those who died without hearing Islam? What does this lesson teach you about trusting His wisdom?
?

?
Imagine you are a parent of a child who dies before reaching the age of accountability. This lesson tells you that such a child will be tested by fire in the afterlife. Does this thought give you peace or grief? What is your heart saying to you right now about Allah's mercy?

Al-Ash'ari's Linguistic Analysis of 'Nazar'
Al-Ash'ari classifies and eliminates two possible meanings of 'nazar'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ash'ari uses linguistic analysis to determine the meaning of 'nazar' in the verse about the beatific vision.

Core Idea
The meaning of 'nazar' in the Quran must fit context and linguistic usage.

Al-Ash'ari begins his argument for the beatific vision by examining the key word 'nazar' in the verse 'Wujuhun yawma'idhin nadirah ila rabbiha nazirah.' He identifies four possible meanings in Arabic and systematically eliminates those inconsistent with the context. This lesson explores his method of linguistic reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once. Then read the translation. Notice the four meanings listed and the arguments that follow.
2
Identify the four meanings
Al-Ash'ari lists four possible meanings: reflection (i'tibar), waiting (intizar), compassion (ta'attuf), and vision (ru'yah). Underline each in the text.
3
Understand the rejection of the first meaning
He rejects 'reflection' because the Hereafter is not a place for reflection. Why? Because reflection involves pondering evidence, but the afterlife is a realm of recompense, not reasoning.
4
Understand the rejection of the second meaning
He rejects 'waiting' because when 'nazar' is mentioned with 'face', it refers to physical sight. He gives a linguistic analogy: when people say 'look with your heart', it means reflection, not eye-sight. Similarly, when 'face' is mentioned, it implies the eyes.
This shows Al-Ash'ari's reliance on Arabic usage.
5
Reflect on the method
Notice how Al-Ash'ari uses linguistic and contextual evidence. This is a pattern in kalam: to interpret ambiguous verses, scholars examine possible meanings and rule out those inconsistent with context and established usage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث الكلام في إثبات رؤية الله تعالى بالأبصار في الآخرة قال الله تعالى: ﴿ وُجُوهٌ يَوْمَذٍ نَاضِرَةُ ) يعني مشرقة، إلى رَبِّهَا نَاظِرَةٌ ) [القيامة : ٢٢ - ٢٣] يعني رائية، وليس يخلـو النظـر مـن وجوه نحـن ذاكروها : ١ - إما أن يكون الله عز وجل عنى نظر الاعتبار، كقوله تعالى: (أفلا يَنظُرُونَ إِلَى الْإِبِلِ كَيْفَ خُلِقَتْ ﴾ [ الغاشية : ١٧] . ٢- أو يكون عنى نظر الانتظار كقوله تعالى: ﴿ مَا يَنظُرُونَ إِلَّا صَيْحَةً وَاحِدَةً ) [يس: ٤٩] . -٣- أو أن يكون عنى نظر التعطف، كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا يَنظُرُ إِلَيْهِمْ يَوْمَ القيامة ) [آل عمران: ٧٧] . ٤ - أو يكون عنى نظر الرؤية . فلا يجوز أن يكون الله عز وجل عنى نظر التفكير والاعتبار ؛ لأن الآخرة ليست بدار اعتبار . ولا يجوز أن يكون عنى نظر الانتظار ؛ لأن النظر إذا ذكر مع ذكر الوجه، فمعناه نظر العينين اللتين في الوجه ، كما إذا ذكر أهل اللسان نظر القلب فقالوا : انظر في هذا الأمر بقلبك ، لم يكن معناه نظر العينين، ولذلك إذا ذكر
Chapter Three: The Speech on Affirming the Vision of Allah, the Exalted, with the Eyes in the Hereafter. Allah the Exalted said: {Faces on that day are radiant} meaning shining, {towards their Lord looking} [Al-Qiyamah 75:22-23] meaning seeing. And the word 'looking' (nazar) does not lack aspects that we will mention: 1. Either Allah, Mighty and Majestic, meant the look of reflection (nazar al-i'tibar), as in His saying: {Do they not look at the camels, how they are created?} [Al-Ghashiyah 88:17]. 2. Or He meant the look of waiting (nazar al-intizar), as in His saying: {They do not wait except for a single blast} [Ya-Sin 36:49]. 3. Or He meant the look of compassion (nazar at-ta'attuf), as in His saying: {And He will not look at them on the Day of Resurrection} [Aal Imran 3:77]. 4. Or He meant the look of vision (nazar ar-ru'yah). It is not permissible that Allah, Mighty and Majestic, meant the look of reflection and consideration, because the Hereafter is not a realm of reflection. And it is not permissible that He meant the look of waiting, because when 'looking' (nazar) is mentioned alongside the mention of the face, its meaning is the looking of the two eyes that are in the face, just as when the people of language mention the look of the heart, they say: 'Look into this matter with your heart,' it does not mean the looking of the two eyes. Therefore, when mentioned...
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter on the vision of Allah in the afterlife. Al-Ash'ari starts by citing the Quranic verse 'Wujuhun yawma'idhin nadirah ila rabbiha nazirah' and interprets 'nazirah' as 'seeing' (ra'iyah). He then systematically lists four possible meanings of the word 'nazar' in Arabic: reflection (i'tibar), waiting (intizar), compassion (ta'attuf), and vision (ru'yah). He argues that the first two are impossible in this context. The meaning of reflection is rejected because the afterlife is not a place for reflection. The meaning of waiting is rejected because the word 'nazar' when paired with 'face' refers specifically to physical sight, not mental anticipation. He supports this with a linguistic analogy: when the heart is mentioned, 'looking' means reflection, but when the face is mentioned, it refers to the eyes. The passage cuts off while he is likely continuing to reject compassion and affirm vision.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some interpret 'nazar' in the verse as 'waiting' or 'reflection', thinking these meanings are possible in the context.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari shows that both meanings are contextually invalid: reflection cannot occur in the Hereafter, and waiting does not fit the pairing with 'face', which indicates physical sight.

Checkpoint
Why does al-Ash'ari reject the interpretation of 'nazar' as 'waiting' (intizar) in the verse?
A) Because waiting only applies to the heart.
B) Because the verse mentions the face, and 'nazar' with the face means vision by the eyes.
C) Because waiting is impossible in the afterlife.
D) Because the word 'nazar' never means waiting in Arabic.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's linguistic analysis shows that 'nazar' in the verse must mean 'seeing by the eyes' because alternative meanings are contextually invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you genuinely live with the certainty that you will one day see Allah with your own eyes—not as an abstract belief, but as a reality that shapes how you speak, act, and prioritize? If not, what would it take for you to make this truth urgent today?
?
Al-Ash'ari argues that the Hereafter is not a place for reflection, meaning this life is your only chance to ponder and act. Are you wasting this opportunity on distractions, or are you actively reflecting on Allah's signs to prepare for that vision? What one habit can you change starting now?
?
If the greatest blessing in the afterlife is seeing your Lord, does your current longing for Allah match the intensity of that promise? When do you last recall feeling genuine, aching desire for His vision—and what does that say about your spiritual state? Will you pray today for that longing to increase?
