باب في الرؤية : احتجت المعتزلة في أن الله عز وجل لا يُرى بالأبصار بقوله تعالى: ﴿ لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الأَبْصَرُ وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الأَبْصَرَ) [الأنعام: ۱۰۳] وقالوا فلما عطف الله عز وجل بقوله: ﴿وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الأَبْصَرَ على قوله: ﴿ لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ ) ، وكان قوله: ﴿وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الْأَبْصَرَ) على العموم أنه يدركها في الدنيا والآخرة، وأنه يراها في الدنيا والآخرة، كان قوله: (لا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ ) دليلاً على أنه لا تراه الأبصار في الدنيا والآخرة، وكان في العموم قوله: ﴿وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الأَبْصَرَ ؛ لأن أحد الكلامين معطوف على الآخر . قيل لهم : فيجب إذا كان عموم القولين واحداً، وكانت الأبصار أبصار العيون وأبصار القلوب؛ لأن الله عزّ وجل قال: ﴿فَإِنَّهَا لَا تَعْمَى الأَبْصَرُ وَلَكِن تَعْمَى الْقُلُوبُ الَّتي في الصُّدُور ﴾ [الحج : ٤٦] ، وقال : أَوْلِي الْأَيْدِى وَالْأَبْصَرِ ) [ص:٤٥] فأراد أبصار القلوب وهي التي يفضل بها المؤمنون الكافرين . ويقول أهل اللغة : فلان بصير بصناعته، يريدون بصر العلم، ويقولون: قـد أبصرته بقلبي، كما يقولون قد أبصرته بعيني، فإذا كان البصر بـصـر الـعـيـون وبصر القلوب ثم أوجبوا علينا أن يكون قوله تعالى: (لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ) في العموم كقوله: ﴿وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الأَبْصَرَ لأن أحد الكلامين معطوف على الآخر، وجب عليهم بحجتهم أن الله عز وجل لا يُدرك بأبصار العيون ولا بأبصار القلوب؛ لأن قوله: (لا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ ) في العموم كقوله : ( وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الأَبْصَرَ) وإذا لم يكن عندهم هكذا فقد وجب أن يكون قوله: ﴿لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ ) أخص من قوله: ﴿وَهُوَ يُدْرِكَ الأبصر وانتقض احتجاجهم . وقيل لهم : إنكم زعمتم أنه لو كان قوله : لا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ) خاصاً في وقت دون وقت لكان قوله : ( وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الأَبْصَرَ) خاصاً في وقت دون وقت، وكان قوله : لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ ) [الشورى: ۱۱]، وقوله: ﴿ لَا تَأْخُذُهُ سِنَةٌ وَلَا نَوْمٌ ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٥٥] ، وقوله : ( لَا يَظْلِمُ النَّاسَ شَيْئًا ﴾ [يونس : ٤٤] في وقت دون وقت، فإن جعلتم قوله تعالى: لا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ) خاصاً رجع احتجاجكم عليكم، وقيل لكم: إذا كان قوله : لا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ) خاصاً ولم يجب خصوص هذه الآيات، فلم أنكرتم أن يكون قوله عز وجل لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ ) إنما أراد في الدنيا دون الآخرة؟ كما أن قوله: لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ ) أراد بعض الأبصار دون بعض، ولا يوجب ذلك تخصيص هذه الآيات التي عارضتمونا بها . فإن قالوا: قوله تعالى: ﴿ لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ ) يوجب أن لا يدرك بها في الدنيا والآخرة، وليس ينفي ذلك أن نراه بقلوبنا، ونبصره بها، ولا ندركه بها . قيل لهم : فما أنكرتم أن يكون لا تدركه بأبصار العيون، ولا يوجب إذا لم ندركه بها أن لا نراه ونبصره بها فرؤيتنا له بالعيون وإبصارنا له بها ليس بإدراك لـه بها، كما أن إبصارنا له بالقلوب ورؤيتنا له بها ليس بإدراك له بها . فإن قالوا رؤية البصر هي إدراك البصر قيل لهم : ما الفرق بينكم وبين من قال : إن رؤية القلب وإبصاره هو إدراكه وإحاطته، فإذا كان علم القلب بالله عز وجل وإبصار القلب له ورؤيته إياه ليس بإحاطة ولا إدراك، فما أنكرتم أن تكون رؤية العيون وإبصارها الله عز وجل ليس بإحاطة ولا إدراك .
Chapter on Seeing (ar-Ru'ya). The Mu'tazila argued that Allah, Mighty and Majestic, is not seen by eyes (al-absar) based on His statement: 'Vision does not perceive Him, and He perceives vision' (Surah al-An'am 6:103). They said: Since Allah, Mighty and Majestic, joined His statement 'and He perceives vision' to His statement 'Vision does not perceive Him', and His statement 'and He perceives vision' is general that He perceives it in this world and the Hereafter, and that He sees it in this world and the Hereafter, then His statement 'Vision does not perceive Him' is evidence that vision (al-absar) does not see Him in this world and the Hereafter, and His statement 'and He perceives vision' is general because one of the two statements is conjoined to the other. It was said to them: Then, if the generality of the two statements is one, and vision (al-absar) includes both the vision of eyes and the vision of hearts, because Allah, Mighty and Majestic, said: 'For indeed they are not blind of the eyes, but the hearts within the breasts are blind' (Surah al-Hajj 22:46), and He said: '[He] of hands and vision' (Surah Sad 38:45), by which He meant the vision of hearts, by which the believers are distinguished from the disbelievers. And the people of language say: 'So-and-so is perspicacious (basir) in his craft', meaning the vision of knowledge, and they say: 'I have perceived him (abṣartuhu) with my heart', just as they say: 'I have seen him (abṣartuhu) with my eye.' So if vision (al-basar) is vision of eyes and vision of hearts, and then they required us that His statement 'Vision does not perceive Him' is general like His statement 'and He perceives vision' because one of the two statements is conjoined to the other, it would be necessary for them according to their argument that Allah, Mighty and Majestic, is not perceived by vision of eyes nor by vision of hearts, because His statement 'Vision does not perceive Him' is in generality like His statement 'and He perceives vision'. And if it is not so according to them, then it would be necessary that His statement 'Vision does not perceive Him' is more specific than His statement 'and He perceives vision', and their argument would be invalidated. And it was said to them: You claimed that if His statement 'Vision does not perceive Him' were specific to a time without a time, then His statement 'and He perceives vision' would be specific to a time without a time, and His statement 'There is nothing like unto Him' (Surah ash-Shura 42:11), and His statement 'Neither slumber nor sleep overtakes Him' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:255), and His statement 'God does not wrong people at all' (Surah Yunus 10:44) would be [specific] to a time without a time. If you make His statement 'Vision does not perceive Him' specific, then your argument would turn against you, and it would be said to you: If His statement 'Vision does not perceive Him' is specific and the specificity of these verses is not required, then why do you deny that His statement, Mighty and Majestic, 'Vision does not perceive Him' meant only in this world and not the Hereafter? Just as His statement 'Vision does not perceive Him' meant some vision (absar) without others, and that does not necessitate the specification of these verses which you have used against us. If they say: His statement 'Vision does not perceive Him' necessitates that He is not perceived by it in this world and the Hereafter, and that does not negate that we see Him with our hearts and perceive Him by them, but we do not perceive (nudrik) Him by them. It was said to them: Then why do you deny that He is not perceived by the eyes, and if we do not perceive (nudrik) Him by them, that does not necessitate that we do not see (nara) Him and perceive (nubṣiruhu) Him by them? For our seeing (ru'yatuna) of Him with the eyes and our perceiving (ibṣaruna) Him by them is not an act of perception (idrak) of Him by them, just as our perceiving (ibṣaruna) Him with hearts and our seeing (ru'yatuna) Him by them is not an act of perception (idrak) of Him by them. If they say: Seeing (ru'ya) of the eye is the perception (idrak) of the eye, it is said to them: What is the difference between you and one who says: Seeing (ru'ya) of the heart and its perception (ibṣar) is its grasping (idrak) and encompassing (ihata)? For if the knowledge of the heart of Allah, Mighty and Majestic, and the heart's perception (ibṣar) of Him and its seeing (ru'ya) of Him is not encompassing (ihata) nor perception (idrak), then why do you deny that seeing (ru'ya) of the eyes and their perception (ibṣar) of Allah, Mighty and Majestic, is not encompassing (ihata) nor perception (idrak)?
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila's argument against the possibility of seeing Allah (ar-ru'ya) based on the verse 'La tudrikuhu al-absar' (Vision does not perceive Him). Al-Ash'ari presents the Mu'tazila's proof: they argue that because the verse says 'does not perceive Him' and is conjoined with 'and He perceives vision' which is general for both worlds, the negation is also general for both worlds. Al-Ash'ari then refutes this by first pointing out that 'absar' in the Quran can refer to both eyes and hearts, citing verses where 'absar' means insight. He argues that if the Mu'tazila insist on the general application of the negation, then it would also negate perception by hearts, which they do not hold. Therefore, their argument is inconsistent. He further argues that if they claim the negation is specific (to eyes or to this world), then their own argument collapses. The Mu'tazila then shift to argue that the negation of idrak does not negate ru'ya with hearts. Al-Ash'ari responds that if ru'ya with hearts is not idrak, then ru'ya with eyes can also be not idrak. He challenges the Mu'tazila's claim that ru'ya of the eye is necessarily idrak, pointing out that ru'ya of the heart is not idrak or ihata, so ru'ya of the eyes need not be either. The key distinction is between ru'ya (seeing) and idrak (perception/grasping). The Mu'tazila conflate them; Al-Ash'ari separates them, allowing for seeing Allah without encompassing Him.

Key Terms
الرؤية
الإدراك
الإحاطة
العيون
القلوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila equated ru'ya with idrak for the eyes but not for the heart.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari shows that ru'ya and idrak are distinct: ru'ya can occur without idrak, both for eyes and hearts.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Ash'ari, what is the relationship between ru'ya (seeing) and idrak (perceiving)?
A) Ru'ya is always the same as idrak.
B) Ru'ya can occur without idrak.
C) Idrak is a prerequisite for ru'ya.
D) Ru'ya is only for the heart, idrak is only for the eye.

Key Takeaway
The verse 'La tudrikuhu al-absar' negates full comprehension of Allah, not the act of seeing Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe you know Allah, but is your knowledge tainted by an assumption that you must fully comprehend Him? Where in your life do you demand exhaustive answers from Allah instead of trusting His revelation? What will you do today to surrender your need for complete understanding?
?
The Mu'tazila insisted that seeing must involve full perception, and they used that to deny the beatific vision. Are there any theological positions you hold simply because you assume a certain human capacity must apply to Allah? Examine your heart: is there any attribute of Allah you've limited because you cannot imagine it otherwise?
?
Al-Ash'ari shows that the heart can see Allah without encompassing Him. Do you experience a genuine sense of Allah's presence and majesty in your worship, or have you reduced your connection to mere intellectual assent? What concrete step will you take this week to cultivate a heart-vision of Allah that does not demand full comprehension?

Refuting the Claim that 'Vision Perceives Him Not' is Absolute
Refutation using conditional logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ash'ari uses logical refutation to show that the verse about vision can be specific, thus not denying the beatific vision in the Hereafter.

Core Idea
The verse's specificity undermines the opponent's absolute claim.

In this passage, Imam Ash'ari engages in a crisp dialectical refutation. He takes the opponent's own assumption—that the verse is specific—and turns it against them. This lesson will unpack his clever reasoning, showing how a crucial verse about Allah's visibility admits of interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'If you make... then your argument returns against you.'
The key move is turning the opponent's logic against them.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
The opponent asserts that the verse 'La tudrikuhu al-absar' is absolute and general, denying any vision of Allah. Ash'ari challenges this by showing that if they accept it can be specific in some sense, then it could be specific to this world.
3
Understand the logical refutation
Ash'ari argues: if the verse is specific (as the opponent might concede to explain other verses), then it could be specific to this world. Thus, it does not negate vision in the Hereafter. This refutes their original claim.
The argument is a classic reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن جعلتم قوله تعالى: ﴿ لا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ ﴾ خاصاً رجع احتجاجكم عليكم، وقيل لكم: إذا كان قوله: ﴿ لا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ ﴾ خاصاً ولم يجب خصوص هذه الآيات، فلم أنكرتم أن يكون قوله عز وجل ﴿ لا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ ﴾ إنما أراد في الدنيا دون الآخرة؟ كما أن قوله: ﴿ لا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ ﴾ أراد بعض الأبصار دون بعض، ولا يوجب ذلك تخصيص هذه الآيات التي عارضتمونا بها.
Then if you make the saying of the Exalted "Vision perceives Him not" specific, your argument returns against you, and it is said to you: If His saying "Vision perceives Him not" is specific and the specificity of these verses is not necessary, then why do you deny that His saying "Vision perceives Him not" might mean in this world only and not in the Hereafter? Just as His saying "Vision perceives Him not" meant some visions without others, and that does not necessitate the specification of these verses with which you opposed us.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (jadal) of the opponent who asserts that verse "لا تدركه الأبصار" is general and prohibits seeing Allah in the Hereafter. The author turns their own logic against them: if they claim the verse is specific (e.g., to some eyes or this world), then their argument collapses. The author argues that the verse could be specific to this world, just as other verses are specific, and thus does not prove the negation of vision in the Hereafter. The key move is to show that the opponent's assumption of generality is not forced by the text.

Key Terms
إدراك
بصَر
خاص
عام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'La tudrikuhu al-absar' is absolutely general and prohibits any vision of Allah in any context.
Correction: The verse could be specific to this world or to certain eyes, thus not necessarily negating the beatific vision in the Hereafter.

Checkpoint
What is the central logical move in Ash'ari's refutation?
A) He argues the verse is metaphorical.
B) He shows that if the verse is specific, it could be specific to this world.
C) He claims the verse is abrogated.
D) He cites consensus on vision.

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari refutes the claim that the verse negates vision of Allah by showing it can be specific to this world, thus preserving the possibility of seeing Allah in the Hereafter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever clung to a single Qur'anic verse as absolute proof for a belief about Allah, without considering the possibility that it might be specific to a context? What would it cost you to admit that your interpretation might be limited?
?
This lesson shows that logical consistency demands we apply the same hermeneutic rules to all verses. In your own understanding of Islam, are there areas where you apply a stricter standard to others' arguments than to your own? How can you cultivate intellectual humility before Allah's speech?
?
If the opponent's absolute denial of seeing Allah in the Hereafter is based on a potentially specific verse, what does that say about the danger of making definitive claims about the unseen? Are there any of your own certainties about the afterlife that might need re-examination?

Distinguishing Vision from Perception
Response to an objection about heart-vision vs. eye-vision

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the critical distinction between ru'ya (vision) and idrak (perception) in the debate about seeing Allah, and how this resolves the objection based on the verse.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah is not the same as perceiving Him.

An opponent concedes that the verse 'Vision perceives Him not' negates perception in both worlds, but they try to allow heart-vision, claiming the verse only addresses eyes. The author replies by drawing a crucial distinction: vision (ru'ya) and perception (idrak) are not identical. Just as heart-vision is admitted without perception, eye-vision could also be vision without perception. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the opponent's claim: the verse negates perception by eyes in both worlds, but does not negate seeing with hearts. Identify their concession and their attempted loophole.
The opponent agrees that perception (idrak) is negated, but they think 'seeing' (ru'ya) with hearts is still possible.
2
Follow the author's reply
The author turns the tables: if heart-vision is not perception, why cannot eye-vision also be vision without perception? The verse only negates perception, not vision itself.
The key move is separating the concept of 'seeing' from 'perceiving/encompassing'.
3
Compare the two cases
Notice the parallel drawn: just as heart-vision is not perception, eye-vision might also not be perception. The verse does not forbid seeing (ru'ya), only perceiving (idrak).
4
Reflect on the doctrinal significance
This distinction allows affirming that believers will see Allah in the Hereafter (as per Sunni creed) without contradicting the verse, because seeing is not the same as perceiving.
Imam al-Ash'ari uses this argument to defend the vision of Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: قوله تعالى: ﴿ لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ ﴾ يوجب أن لا يدرك بها في الدنيا والآخرة، وليس ينفي ذلك أن نراه بقلوبنا، ونبصره بها، ولا ندركه بها.
قيل لهم : فما أنكرتم أن يكون لا تدركه بأبصار العيون، ولا يوجب إذا لم ندركه بها أن لا نراه ونبصره بها فرؤيتنا له بالعيون وإبصارنا له بها ليس بإدراك له بها، كما أن إبصارنا له بالقلوب ورؤيتنا له بها ليس بإدراك له بها.
If they say: The saying of the Exalted "Vision perceives Him not" necessitates that He is not perceived by vision in this world and the Hereafter, but that does not negate that we see Him with our hearts and see Him thereby without perceiving Him thereby. It is said to them: Why do you deny that it is "not perceived by the eyes of the eyes" and does not necessitate that if we do not perceive Him thereby, we do not see Him and behold Him thereby? For our vision of Him with the eyes and our beholding Him thereby is not a perception of Him thereby, just as our beholding Him with hearts and our vision of Him thereby is not a perception of Him thereby.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The opponent concedes that the verse negates perception in both worlds but tries to allow heart-vision, claiming the verse only addresses eyes. The author replies by analogy: if heart-vision is not perception (as they agree), then eye-vision might also be vision without perception. Therefore, the verse does not negate seeing Allah with the eyes, as long as that seeing is not perceived (encompassed). The distinction between ru'ya (seeing) and idrak (perceiving/encompassing) is key.

Key Terms
رؤية
إدراك
بصَر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the verse 'Vision perceives Him not' proves that Allah cannot be seen at all, either in this world or the Hereafter, confusing vision with perception.
Correction: The verse only negates perceptual encompassing (idrak), not the act of seeing (ru'ya). The author shows that seeing can occur without perception.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the relationship between eye-vision and perception?
A) Eye-vision always involves perception.
B) Eye-vision does not necessarily entail perception, just as heart-vision does not.
C) Eye-vision is only possible in the Hereafter.
D) Eye-vision is identical to heart-vision.

Key Takeaway
The verse 'Vision perceives Him not' does not negate seeing Allah with eyes or hearts, because seeing (ru'ya) is distinct from perceiving (idrak).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you secretly believe that seeing Allah would mean fully comprehending Him? What does this passage demand you release about your own need to 'grasp' God before you can be satisfied in His presence? How would you live differently today if you truly accepted seeing without fully understanding?
?
If you are unsettled by the idea that we will see Allah without perceiving Him, what does that reveal about your trust in His revelation versus your own desire for control? Are you willing to encounter Allah on His terms, or do you insist on terms that feel safe to your intellect?
?
How does the distinction between ru'ya and idrak challenge your tendency to reduce God to what you can mentally or emotionally encompass? What would it mean for you to accept seeing Him without having to understand Him fully? Write one way this truth changes how you approach worship today.

The Claim That Eye-Vision Is Perception Refuted
Refutation of the equation of eye-vision with perception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author argues that eye-vision of Allah does not necessarily imply perception, based on the analogy with heart-vision.

Core Idea
Vision does not always mean perception; heart-vision proves it.

In this passage, the author engages with an opponent who claims that seeing with the eyes must be a form of perception. The author counters by drawing attention to the heart's vision of Allah, which is agreed to be without encompassing or full perception. This refutes the opponent's assumption and establishes that divine vision is not necessarily perceptual.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The opponent argues that eye-vision is perception. Read the Arabic and translation carefully.
Notice the direct claim: 'رؤية البصر هي إدراك البصر'.
2
Analyze the refutation
The author uses the heart's vision as a counterexample. The heart knows Allah but does not encompass Him. This shows that vision can exist without perception.
The rhetorical question 'ما الفرق بينكم وبين من قال' highlights the inconsistency.
3
Understand the logical structure
The argument is by analogy: if heart-vision is not perception, then eye-vision need not be either. The opponent is forced to accept consistency.
This is a common argumentative technique in kalam.
4
Reflect on the implication
This shows that seeing Allah in the afterlife does not imply limitation or full encompassing, preserving His transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا رؤية البصر هي إدراك البصر
قيل لهم : ما الفرق بينكم وبين من قال : إن رؤية القلب وإبصاره هو إدراكه وإحاطته، فإذا كان علم القلب بالله عز وجل وإبصار القلب له ورؤيته إياه ليس بإحاطة ولا إدراك، فما أنكرتم أن تكون رؤية العيون وإبصارها الله عز وجل ليس بإحاطة ولا إدراك.
If they say: Vision of the eye is perception of the eye. It is said to them: What is the difference between you and the one who says that the heart's vision and sight is its perception and encompassing? So if the heart's knowledge of Allah, its sight and vision of Him is not an encompassing nor a perception, then why do you deny that the eyes' vision and sight of Allah is not an encompassing nor a perception?
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is another objection-and-answer. The opponent asserts that eye-vision inherently means perception (idrak). The author refutes by consistency: the opponent already agrees that heart-vision (knowledge of Allah) is not perception or encompassing (ihata). If heart-vision is not perception, then there is no reason to insist that eye-vision must be. This undermines the opponent's position by highlighting their inconsistency.

Key Terms
إحاطة
إدراك
رؤية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All vision inherently involves perception or encompassing.
Correction: The author demonstrates through the analogy of heart-vision that vision can exist without perception.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main argument in this passage?
A) The heart's vision is perception, so eye-vision must be too.
B) The heart's vision is not perception, so eye-vision may also not be.
C) The verse is unclear about heart-vision.
D) The opponents are ignorant of language.

Key Takeaway
Eye-vision of Allah does not imply perception, just as heart-vision does not.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that seeing Allah on the Day of Judgment will not fully encompass Him? How does that affect your longing for that vision?
?
If heart-vision (knowledge) of Allah does not mean you have fully grasped Him, does your current knowledge of Allah make you humble or arrogant? Are you content with not fully knowing Him?
?
When you imagine seeing Allah, do you instinctively think of limiting Him? What must you correct in your heart to align with this teaching?

Parallelism of the Two Verses Is Refuted
Logical refutation of parallelism claim using reductio

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari refutes the claim that the two verses are parallel in generality by exposing the absurd consequences of the opponent's logic.

Core Idea
The parallel structure of the verses does not imply equal meaning; it leads to absurdity.

Imam al-Ash'ari presents a sharp logical argument to dismantle the opponent's interpretation of the two verses. By forcing the opponent to admit certain constraints, he reveals that their claim of parallelism cannot hold. This lesson walks through the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and English translation. Observe the dialogue format.
The author uses a question-and-answer structure.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
The opponent says the two verses are equal in generality because they are conjoined. Note this assumption.
3
Follow the reductio reasoning
The author first gets the opponent to admit that the first verse negates all perception. Then asks if the second verse implies physical perception. The opponent denies.
This inconsistency disproves the claim of equal generality.
4
Understand the conclusion
Realize that the parallelism does not force identical meaning; the verses apply to different subjects.
The refutation shows the danger of assuming grammatical coordination implies semantic equality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال لهم : إذا كان قول الله عز وجل: ﴿ لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ ﴾ في العموم كقوله: ﴿ وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الْأَبْصَرَ ﴾ لأن أحد الكلامين معطوف على الآخر، فخبرونا أليس الأبصار والعيون لا تدركه رؤية ولا لمساً ولا ذوقاً ولا على وجه من الوجوه؟
فمن قولهم : نعم، فيقال لهم : أخبرونا عن قوله عز وجل: ﴿ وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الْأَبْصَرَ ﴾ أتزعمون أنه يدركها لمساً وذوقاً بأن يلمسها؟ فمن قولهم : لا ، فيقال لهم : فقد انتقض قولكم : إن قوله : ﴿ وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الْأَبْصَرَ ﴾ في العموم كقوله : ﴿ لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ ﴾
And it is said to them: If the saying of Allah "Vision perceives Him not" is in generality like His saying "and He perceives the visions" because one of the two sayings is coordinated with the other, then inform us: do not visions and eyes not perceive Him by sight, touch, taste, or in any way? They will say: Yes. Then it is said to them: Inform us about His saying "and He perceives the visions" – do you claim that He perceives them by touch and taste by touching them? They will say: No. Then it is said to them: Your statement has been refuted: that His saying "and He perceives the visions" is in generality like His saying "Vision perceives Him not."
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a logical refutation using a reductio ad absurdum. The opponent claims the two verses are equal in generality (umum). The author gets them to admit that visions do not perceive Allah in any physical way (sight, touch, taste). Then the author asks: if the second verse is equally general, does that mean Allah perceives visions by touch and taste? They deny this, so their claim of parallelism collapses. Thus, the first verse cannot be taken to have a general negative sense against vision in the Hereafter.

Key Terms
عموم
عطف
إدراك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That conjoined verses always have the same level of generality
Correction: The verses are conjoined but the first negates all perception, while the second uses the same verb for Allah’s perception, which cannot include physical means.

Checkpoint
What conclusion does the author draw from the opponent's admission about 'وهو يدرك الأبصار'?
A) It confirms the opponent's view.
B) The opponent's claim of parallelism is refuted.
C) The verse means Allah sees visions.
D) The verse is not in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The parallelism of the two verses does not mean they have the same scope; the first negates all perception, while the second attributes perception to Allah without implying physical senses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'Vision perceives Him not', do you truly internalize that Allah is beyond any sensory grasp? What comfortable, human-like image of Allah have you unknowingly held, and how will this logical proof help you purify your belief?
?
The opponent’s error was letting grammatical structure override the context and clear meaning. In your own study of the Quran, where might you be too rigid in applying a rule without considering the deeper intent? What is one verse you will re-examine today to ensure you understand it in its proper light?
?
If you were to defend the transcendence of Allah (tanzih) against someone who anthropomorphizes based on parallel verses, would you be prepared to use this logical argument? Commit to memorizing the steps of this refutation so you can uphold Allah’s majesty with clarity.

The Meaning of 'He Perceives the Visions'
Question and opponent's interpretation of a key verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari uses the opponents' own interpretation of 'idrak' to argue against their literalist view.

Core Idea
The opponents themselves interpret 'idrak' as knowledge, not physical sight.

Imam al-Ash'ari challenges his opponents to explain the meaning of the Qur'anic phrase 'He perceives the visions.' Their answer reveals a crucial point: they interpret 'idrak' as knowledge, undermining their earlier insistence on a literal, physical meaning. This lesson examines that exchange.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: a question followed by the opponents' answer.
The passage is short but packed with implication.
2
Identify the question and answer
What does al-Ash'ari ask? How do the opponents respond? Write down the key terms: إدراك and علم.
3
Notice the opponents' concession
The opponents say 'meaning that He knows them.' This shows they interpret 'idrak' as knowledge here, not physical perception. Why is this significant?
Think about their earlier arguments.
4
Reflect on the argumentative strategy
Al-Ash'ari uses the opponents' own words to show inconsistency. If they accept a non-literal meaning here, they cannot insist on literalism elsewhere.
This is a common dialectical technique in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال لهم : حدثونا عن قول الله عز وجل: ﴿ وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الْأَبْصَرَ ﴾ ما
فإن قالوا : معنى يُدْرِكُ الْأَبْصَرَ أنه يعلمها .
And it is said to them: Inform us about the saying of Allah "and He perceives the visions" – what (meaning)? If they say: The meaning of "He perceives the visions" is that He knows them.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage begins a new line of questioning. The author asks the opponents to explain the meaning of 'يدرك الأبصار' (He perceives the visions). The opponents are recorded as saying it means 'He knows them' (ya'lamuha). This answer reveals that they themselves interpret 'idrak' in this context as knowledge, not physical perception. This is a key concession that undermines their earlier literal interpretation of 'idrak' in the first verse. The author's subsequent response (not fully preserved here) would likely use this against them.

Key Terms
إدراك
علم
بصَر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'idrak' always means physical sight.
Correction: The opponents themselves interpret 'idrak' in this verse as knowledge, showing that it can have a metaphorical meaning.

Checkpoint
How do the opponents interpret 'يدرك الأبصار'?
A) He sees them.
B) He knows them.
C) He touches them.
D) He creates them.

Key Takeaway
The opponents' concession that 'idrak' means knowledge in this verse weakens their literalist position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a verse of the Quran that challenges your existing understanding, do you force an interpretation that fits your comfort (like the opponents did) or do you pause and submit? What verse has recently challenged you, and how did you respond?
?
The opponents here were inconsistent: they allowed a non-literal meaning here but insisted on literalism elsewhere. Where in your own life do you apply double standards—interpreting some teachings flexibly for yourself but demanding strictness from others? Be specific and make a concrete intention to rectify this.

Proof that the Quran is Uncreated from the Distinction of Creation and Command
al-Ash'ari presents a linguistic-theological proof for the uncreatedness of the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari uses the Qur'anic verse 'أَلَا لَهُ الْخَلْقُ وَالْأَمْرُ' to prove that the Quran, being Allah's command, is uncreated.

Core Idea
When Allah mentions 'creation' and 'command' separately, the command is distinct from creation and thus uncreated.

This lesson examines Imam al-Ash'ari's scriptural proof that the Quran is uncreated. Building on the principle that general words must be interpreted generally unless evidence specifies otherwise, he argues that Allah separates 'the command' from 'creation' in the verse, showing that the command (which includes the Quran) is not part of creation. This argument relies on the linguistic principle of 'umum al-lafz' (generality of wording).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the two verses
Read the Arabic passage once. Identify the two Qur'anic verses cited: Surah ar-Rum:25 and Surah al-A'raf:54.
The first verse establishes that Allah's command is His speech.
2
Understand the linguistic principle of 'umum al-lafz'
Notice how al-Ash'ari states that general wording must be taken in its general sense unless there is proof to restrict it. This principle is crucial to the argument.
3
Trace the logical conclusion that the command is separate from creation
Follow the reasoning: 'creation' is general, but 'command' is mentioned separately in the second verse, so it is not part of creation. Thus Allah's command is uncreated.
The Quran is identified as Allah's command, so it is uncreated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن سأل سائل عن الدليل على أن القرآن كلام الله غير مخلوق. قيل له : الدليل على ذلك قوله عز وجل: (وَمِنْ آيَاتِهِ أَنْ تَقُومَ السَّمَاءُ وَالْأَرْضُ بِأَمْرِهِ ) [ الروم : ٢٥) وأمر الله هو كلامه وقوله، فلما أمرهما بالقيام فقامتا لا تهويان؟ كان قيامهما بأمره . وقال عز وجل : ( أَلَا لَهُ الْخَلْقُ وَالْأَمْرُ ﴾ [الأعراف:٥٤]، فالخلق جميع ما خلق داخل فيه ؛ لأن الكلام إذا كان لفظه لفظاً عاماً فحقيقته أنه عام، ولا يجوز لنا أن نزيل الكلام عن حقيقته بغير حجة ولا برهان، فلما قال: ﴿أَلَا لَهُ الخَلْقُ ) كان هذا في جميع الخلق، ولما قال: ﴿وَالأمر ذكر أمراً غير جميع الخلق، فدل ما وصفنا على أن أمر الله غير مخلوق.
If a questioner asks for evidence that the Quran is the speech of Allah, uncreated, it is said to him: The evidence for that is His statement, Mighty and Majestic: (And among His signs is that the heaven and the earth stand by His command) [ar-Rum: 25]. And Allah's command is His speech and His word. When He commanded them to stand, they stood, not falling; their standing was by His command. And He said, Mighty and Majestic: (Unquestionably, His is the creation and the command) [al-A'raf: 54]. So creation includes everything created, because when speech has a general wording, its reality is that it is general, and it is not permissible for us to remove the speech from its reality without a proof or evidence. So when He said: (Unquestionably, His is the creation), this applied to all creation, and when He said: (and the command), He mentioned a command other than all creation. Thus what we have described indicates that Allah's command is uncreated.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a scriptural proof that the Quran (the speech of Allah) is uncreated. The author presents two Quranic verses. First, from Surah ar-Rum: 'And among His signs is that the heaven and the earth stand by His command.' Here 'command' (amr) is identified as Allah's speech (kalam). The second verse from al-A'raf: 'Unquestionably, His is the creation and the command.' The argument follows: The word 'creation' (al-khalq) is a general term ('amm) that includes everything Allah has created. As a general term, it must be taken in its general meaning unless there is evidence to specify it. When Allah mentions 'the command' (al-amr) separately after 'creation', it indicates that the command is something other than all creation. Since the Quran is Allah's command, it is therefore not part of creation, i.e., it is uncreated. The author emphasizes that it is not permissible to deviate from the apparent general meaning without a valid proof, and no such proof exists here.

Key Terms
الخلق
الأمر
كلام الله
غير مخلوق
عموم اللفظ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the verse 'أَلَا لَهُ الْخَلْقُ وَالْأَمْرُ' includes the Quran in the general term 'creation', implying the Quran is created.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari argues that 'al-amr' (command) is mentioned distinctly from 'al-khalq' (creation), so it is not included in the general term 'creation' and thus is uncreated.

Checkpoint
What linguistic principle does Imam al-Ash'ari use to separate 'command' from 'creation' in his proof?
A) General wording must be taken generally unless there is evidence to restrict it.
B) The command is eternal and therefore not created.
C) The Quran is speech and speech cannot be created.
D) The verse clearly states that the command is not created.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari proves the Quran's uncreatedness by showing that when Allah mentions 'creation' and 'command' separately in the verse 'أَلَا لَهُ الْخَلْقُ وَالْأَمْرُ', the command (which is the Quran) is not part of creation and is therefore uncreated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you truly believe it is the eternal, uncreated speech of Allah? How does this belief change the way you approach it—will you read it with more reverence and certainty that it is not like any created book?
?
Al-Ash'ari argues that the command is distinct from creation. If the Quran is Allah's command and therefore uncreated, does that affect how you view its authority in your life? Are you treating it as a created human product or as the eternal decree that demands your obedience?
?
The verse 'أَلَا لَهُ الْخَلْقُ وَالْأَمْرُ' separates creation and command. In what areas of your life are you treating Allah's commands as if they were mere creations—subject to change or compromise? What step will you take today to affirm that His command is eternal and uncreated?

Proof that God's Speech is Uncreated by Analogy with His Knowledge
Imam Ashari proves that God's speech is uncreated by analogy with His eternal knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proof that God's speech is uncreated through analogy with His eternal knowledge.

Core Idea
God's speech, like His knowledge, must be eternal — otherwise He could not be speaking.

Imam Ashari uses a powerful analogy to defend the uncreated nature of God's speech. He argues that if speech were created, God would be devoid of speech, just as if knowledge were created, He would be ignorant. Since God is eternally knowing, He must be eternally speaking. This lesson unpacks this reductio ad absurdum argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the full Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Notice the flow of the argument from the example to the analogy.
Pay attention to the parallel structure between speech and knowledge.
2
Understand the reductio on speech
The author first argues that if God's speech were created, God would not be speaking, which is absurd. See how this parallel the argument for knowledge.
3
Grasp the analogy with knowledge
Since God's knowledge is eternal and cannot be created, the same applies to speech. Both are attributes that cannot have opposites attributed to God.
The opposite of speech is silence; the opposite of knowledge is ignorance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفرس وحمار وغير ذلك كلام الله ، وفي هذا ما فيه .
فلما استحال ذلك
صح أن قول الله للأشياء كوني غيرها، وإذا كان غير المخلوقات فقد خرج كلام الله عزّ وجلّ عن أن يكون مخلوقاً، ويلزم من يثبت كلام الله مخلوقاً أن يثبت [أن] الله غير متكلم ولا قائل، وذلك فاسد، كما يفسد أن يكون علم الله مخلوقاً وأن يكون الله غير عالم، فلما كان الله عز وجل لم يزل عالماً، إذ لم يجز أن يكون لم يزل بخلاف العلم موصوفاً، استحال أن يكون لم يزل بخلاف الكلام موصوفاً؛ لأن خلاف الكلام الذي لا يكون معه كلام سكوت أو آفة، كما أن خلاف العلم الذي لا يكون علم جهل أو شك، أو آفة، ويستحيل أن يُوصف ربنا عز وجل بخلاف العلم، ولذلك يستحيل أن يوصف بخلاف الكلام من السكوت والآفات، فوجب لذلك أن يكون لم يزل متكلماً، كما وجب أن يكون لم يزل عالماً
And a horse and a donkey and other than that are the speech of Allah, and in this is what is in it. When that is impossible, it is correct that Allah's saying to things 'Be' is other than them, and if it is other than the created things, then the speech of Allah Almighty has exited from being created. And one who affirms Allah's speech as created is obligated to affirm that Allah is not speaking and not a sayer, and that is corrupt, just as it is corrupt that Allah's knowledge be created and that Allah be not knowing. Since Allah Almighty has not ceased to be knowing, for it is not permissible that He has not ceased to be described with the opposite of knowledge, it is impossible that He has not ceased to be described with the opposite of speech; because the opposite of speech, which is not with it speech, is silence or defect, just as the opposite of knowledge, which is not knowledge, is ignorance or doubt or defect. And it is impossible that our Lord Almighty be described with the opposite of knowledge, and therefore it is impossible that He be described with the opposite of speech, from silence and defects. So it is necessary therefore that He has not ceased to be speaking, just as it is necessary that He has not ceased to be knowing.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a proof by analogy (qiyas) and reductio ad absurdum. The author begins by noting that even ordinary things like a horse and donkey are attributed to Allah's speech (likely a reference to the fact that Allah's command 'Be' applies to all creation). He then argues: if Allah's speech were created, then Allah Himself would not be speaking or saying anything, which is absurd. He parallels this with knowledge: if Allah's knowledge were created, Allah would not be knowing, which is also absurd. Since it is established that Allah has always been knowing (eternally), it must also be that He has always been speaking. The opposite of speech is silence or defect, and the opposite of knowledge is ignorance or doubt—both impossible for Allah. Therefore, Allah is eternally speaking.

Key Terms
كلام الله (kalam Allah)
مخلوق (makhluq)
علم الله (ilm Allah)
لم يزل (lam yazal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that affirming God's speech as uncreated implies multiple eternal entities alongside God.
Correction: The author is only affirming the eternity of an attribute, not a separate entity. God's speech is an attribute of His essence, not a co-eternal being.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Ashari, why must God's speech be eternal?
A) Because He spoke to Moses
B) Because His knowledge is eternal and speech is analogous
C) Because the Quran says so in a specific verse
D) Because speech is not a defect

Key Takeaway
God's speech must be eternal because, just as His knowledge is eternal, He cannot be described with the opposite of speech, such as silence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah is eternally speaking, what does that mean for your attitude when you read or hear the Quran? Do you treat it as the living, eternal address of God to you right now, or as a historical document?
?
The passage argues that Allah cannot be described with silence. Have you ever avoided listening to His speech—by neglecting the Quran or dismissing His signs? What will you change today to truly hear Him?

The Ocean of Ink: Proving the Eternity of God's Speech
Imam Ashari uses Quran 18:109 to argue that God's speech is inexhaustible and eternal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Quran 18:109 is used by Imam Ashari to prove that Allah's speech is eternal and not subject to finitude.

Core Idea
God's speech cannot be exhausted, proving it is eternal and uncreated.

Imam Ashari turns to a powerful Quranic verse to demonstrate that Allah's speech is infinite. If all the seas were ink, they would run out before His words. This vivid imagery not only shows the vastness of divine speech but also its eternal nature, against the Jahmiyya who claimed it was created and finite.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its argument
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the verse sets up a conditional scenario: if the sea were ink, it would be exhausted before the words of Allah.
The verse is from Surah Al-Kahf (18:109).
2
Understand the logical implication
Imam Ashari draws a logical conclusion: if the sea cannot exhaust Allah's words, then His speech is not subject to finitude. This implies that speech cannot end or perish.
Compare with divine knowledge which is also infinite.
3
Connect to divine attributes
If speech could be exhausted, it would imply a defect or silence in Allah, which is impossible. Therefore, Allah has always been speaking (eternal attribute).
The attribute of speech is like knowledge – neither can be finite.
4
Recognize the refutation of Jahmiyya
The Jahmiyya claimed that Allah's speech is created and finite. This verse refutes that by showing it is impossible for His words to be exhausted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال الله عز وجل : ( قُل لَّوْ كَانَ الْبَحْرُ مِدَادًا لِكَلِمَتِ رَبِّي لَنَفِدَ الْبَحْرُ قَبْلَ أَن تَنقَدَ كَلِمَتُ رَبِّي ﴾ [الكهف : ١٠٩] فلو كانت البحار مداداً كتبت لنفدت البحار وتكسرت الأقلام، ولم يلحق الفناء كلمات ربي، كما لا يلحق الفناء علــم الله عز وجل، ومن فني كلامه لحقته الآفات وجرى عليه السكوت، فلما لم يجز ذلك على ربنا عز وجل صح أنه لم يزل متكلماً؛ لأنه لو لم يكن متكلماً، لوجب عليه السكوت والآفات تعالى ربنا عن قول الجهمية علواً كبيراً .
And Allah Almighty said: 'Say, if the sea were ink for the words of my Lord, the sea would be exhausted before the words of my Lord are exhausted.' [Al-Kahf:109] So if the seas were ink and written, the seas would be exhausted and the pens would break, and the words of my Lord would not be overtaken by finitude, just as the knowledge of Allah Almighty is not overtaken by finitude. And whoever's speech perishes, defects overtake him and silence occurs to him. So when that is not permissible for our Lord Almighty, it is correct that He has not ceased to be speaking; because if He were not speaking, silence and defects would be necessary for Him—exalted is our Lord above the saying of the Jahmiyya, a great exaltation.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a scriptural proof from Quran 18:109. Imam Ashari cites the verse where Allah says that if the ocean were ink for His words, the ocean would run out before the words run out. He then argues: if the seas were ink and all writing were done, the words of Allah would not be exhausted. This demonstrates that His speech is not subject to finitude or exhaustion. Exhaustion would imply that His speech could end, which would necessitate silence or defect—attributes impossible for Allah. Therefore, Allah has always been speaking (eternally). He concludes with a condemnation of the Jahmiyya who claim otherwise.

Key Terms
كلمات ربي (kalimat Rabbi)
الفناء (al-fana')
السكوت (al-sukut)
الجهمية (al-Jahmiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse means that Allah's words are many but not necessarily eternal.
Correction: Imam Ashari uses the verse to prove that Allah's words are not subject to finitude, hence they are eternal and uncreated.

Checkpoint
What does Imam Ashari conclude from the verse about the ocean of ink?
A) That God's words are many but can be written
B) That God's words are uncreated and eternal
C) That God's speech is created and finite
D) That the ocean is a metaphor for creation

Key Takeaway
Allah's speech is eternal and not subject to finitude, as demonstrated by the inexhaustibility of His words.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God’s speech is eternal and inexhaustible, what does that mean for how you approach the Quran? Do you read it as a finite book with a fixed meaning, or as an infinite ocean that demands your constant humility and seeking? Will you today begin to read even one verse with the conviction that its depths can never be exhausted?
?
Imam Ashari says that if God were not always speaking, silence would be a defect. How does it change your awareness of God to know that He is always speaking? Does that thought make you more accountable to listen to His words? When you remain silent before His verses, do you realize you are meeting the Eternal Speaker? What will you do tomorrow morning to truly listen?
?
The Jahmiyya claimed God’s speech is created, but the verse proves otherwise. Have you ever internally limited God by thinking His words could be captured or finished? When you memorize a surah or finish a translation, do you feel you have 'done' your duty? Or do you feel the weight of the infinite call to engage with the Speaking Lord? What will you change so that your interaction with the Quran reflects its eternity?

Refuting the Jahmiyya: The Absurdity of a Speaking Tree
Imam Ashari refutes the Jahmiyya claim by reductio ad absurdum, comparing them to Christians and citing a Quranic verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ashari uses logical absurdity to refute the Jahmiyya claim that God's speech was created and dwelled in a tree, exposing the theological error of attributing divine speech to a creature.

Core Idea
If God's speech were in a tree, the tree would be claiming divinity—a clear absurdity.

Imam Ashari confronts a radical deviation of the Jahmiyya sect, who claimed that God's speech—the Quran—was created and temporarily lodged in a tree (the burning bush). In this passage, he exposes the logical consequence of their view: the tree itself would have to be the speaker of 'I am Allah,' reducing their claim to absurdity. He also contrasts them with Christians, showing they went even further.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation. Let the force of the argument come through.
Pay attention to the comparison with Christians at the beginning.
2
Identify the comparison with Christians
Notice how Ashari links the Jahmiyya to the Christians, then shows the Jahmiyya went further by claiming God's speech was created and entered a tree.
This comparison highlights the extreme nature of the Jahmiyya claim.
3
Spot the reductio ad absurdum
Find the logical consequence: if speech is created in a tree, then the tree itself would be the speaker of 'I am Allah.' This is an impossibility.
A created thing cannot claim to be the Creator.
4
Connect the Quranic verse
Read the verse from Surah As-Sajda (32:13) that Ashari cites. It affirms that Allah's word is from Him, not created in a creature.
The verse reinforces that divine speech is uncreated and eternal.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Understand Ashari's final point: just as Allah's knowledge cannot be created in a creature, His speech cannot be created in a tree. This upholds the transcendence of Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : وزعمت الجهمية كما زعمت النصارى ؛ لأن النصارى زعمت أن كلمة الله حواها بطن مريم وزادت الجهمية عليهم ؛ فزعمت أن كلام الله مخلوق حل في شجرة، وكانت الشجرة حاوية له؛ فلزمهم أن تكون الشجرة بذلك الكلام متكلمةً، ووجب عليهم أن مخلوقاً من المخلوقين كلّم موسى صلى الله عليه وسلم، وأن الشجرة قالت: يا موسى إنَّني أنا الله لا إله إلا أنا فاعبدني، فلو كان كلام الله مخلوقاً في شجرة، لكان المخلوق قال : يا موسى إنَّني أنا الله لا إله إلا أنا فاعبدني، وقد قال الله عز وجل: وَلَكِن حَقَّ الْقَوْلُ مِن لَأَمْلَأَنَّ جَهَنَّمَ مِنَ الْجِنَّةِ وَالنَّاسِ أَجْمَعِينَ ﴾ [السجدة : ١٣] . وكلام الله من الله عز وجل لا يجوز أن يكون كلامه الذي هو منه مخلوقاً في شجرة مخلوقة، كما لا يجوز أن يكون علمه الذي هو منه مخلوقاً في غيره، تعالى الله ذلك علواً كبيراً .
Section: And the Jahmiyya claimed just as the Christians claimed; because the Christians claimed that the word of Allah was contained in the womb of Mary, and the Jahmiyya added to them: they claimed that the speech of Allah is created and settled in a tree, and the tree was containing it. So it necessarily follows for them that the tree, by that speech, is speaking, and it is necessary for them that a created thing among the created beings spoke to Moses (peace be upon him), and that the tree said: 'O Moses, indeed I am Allah, there is no god but Me, so worship Me.' For if the speech of Allah were created in a tree, then the created thing would have said: 'O Moses, indeed I am Allah, there is no god but Me, so worship Me.' And Allah Almighty said: 'But the word from Me has been justified: I will surely fill Hell with jinn and people all together.' [As-Sajda:13] And the speech of Allah is from Allah Almighty; it is not permissible that His speech, which is from Him, be created in a created tree, just as it is not permissible that His knowledge, which is from Him, be created in other than Him. Exalted is Allah above that, a great exaltation.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a refutation by reductio ad absurdum. Imam Ashari compares the Jahmiyya to Christians: Christians said the word of Allah (Jesus) was contained in Mary's womb; the Jahmiyya outdid them by claiming that Allah's speech was created and entered a tree (the burning bush from which Moses heard the voice). He then draws the necessary consequence: if the speech were created in the tree, then the tree itself would be speaking and claiming divinity: 'I am Allah.' This would mean a created object is declaring itself to be the Creator—extreme absurdity. Ashari also cites Quran 32:13 to assert that the word of Allah is from Him and cannot be created in a creature, just as His knowledge cannot be created in a creature.

Correction: Ashari shows that if speech were created in the tree, the tree itself would be claiming divinity—an absurdity. Therefore, the speech must be uncreated and directly from Allah.

Key Takeaway
Divine speech cannot be created in a creature, for that would lead to a creature claiming divinity—an impossibility.

Answer to Jahmiyya: God's Speech Cannot Be Created in a Creature
Ashari uses an analogy with God's will to argue against created speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's speech cannot be created in a creature, using the parallel argument with God's will.

Core Idea
God's speech cannot be created in a creature because that would make the creature the speaker.

Imam Ashari refutes the Jahmiyya claim that God's speech was created in a tree by drawing a parallel with God's will. Just as God's will cannot be placed in a creature without that creature becoming the wielder of that will, God's speech cannot be placed in a creature without that creature becoming the speaker. This argument preserves God's transcendence and the uniqueness of His attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the structure: the first part presents the analogy with God's will, and the second part applies it to speech.
2
Identify the analogy
Notice that Ashari begins by stating a parallel: just as it is not permissible for Allah to create His will in a creature, so too it is not permissible to create His speech. The underlying principle is that attributes of Allah cannot become attributes of a creature.
The Jahmiyya claimed Allah's speech was created in a tree (as a sound), but Ashari argues this would make the tree the speaker.
3
Understand the reductio ad absurdum
Ashari then shows the consequence: if Allah created His will in a creature, that creature would be the one willing. Similarly, if Allah created His speech in a creature, that creature would be the one speaking. Both are impossible because it would attribute divine attributes to created beings.
This is a logical argument that shows the Jahmiyya position leads to an absurd conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال لهم : كما لا يجوز أن يخلق الله عز وجل إرادته في بعض المخلوقات، كذلك لا يجوز أن يخلق كلامه في بعض المخلوقات، ولو كانت إرادة الله مخلوقة في بعض المخلوقات، لكان ذلك المخلوق هو المريد بها، وذلك يستحيل .
وكذلك يستحيل أن يخلق الله كلامه في مخلوق؛ لأن هذا يوجب أن ذلك المخلوق متكلم به ويستحيل أن يكون كلام الله عز وجل كلاماً للمخلوق .
And it is said to them: Just as it is not permissible for Allah Almighty to create His will in some created things, likewise it is not permissible for Him to create His speech in some created things. And if the will of Allah were created in some created things, then that created thing would be the one willing by it, and that is impossible. And likewise it is impossible for Allah to create His speech in a created thing; because this necessitates that that created thing is speaking by it, and it is impossible for the speech of Allah Almighty to be speech of a created thing.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is an argument from parallel and reductio ad absurdum. Imam Ashari presents a rebuttal: just as it is impermissible for Allah to create His will in a creature (since that would make the creature the actual wielder of that will), it is equally impermissible to create His speech in a creature. If He did, the creature would become the speaker of that speech, meaning Allah's speech would become the speech of a creation—an impossibility. Therefore, the Jahmiyya claim that Allah's speech was created in the tree is false.

Key Terms
إرادة الله (iradat Allah)
مخلوق (makhluq)
متكلم (mutakallim)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God can create His attributes in creatures without transferring the attribute.
Correction: Ashari shows that if an attribute is created in a creature, the creature becomes the subject of that attribute, which is impossible for divine attributes.

Checkpoint
What analogy does Imam Ashari use to refute the claim that God's speech can be created in a creature?
A) God's knowledge cannot be created
B) God's will cannot be created in a creature
C) God's power cannot be created
D) God's mercy cannot be created

Key Takeaway
God's speech cannot be created in a creature because that would make the creature the speaker, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you truly believe that you are uttering Allah's uncreated speech, not a mere created thing? How does this belief affect the reverence and focus in your recitation? What will you do today to increase your awe of the Quran as Allah's very words?

Proof from Quran That Quran is Not Created
Scriptural proof by implication from Quran 74:25.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ashari uses a Quranic verse to argue that the Quran is not created by equating the claim of creation with the polytheists' claim that it is human speech.

Core Idea
Calling the Quran created equals calling it human speech—which Allah condemned.

Imam Ashari presents a concise scriptural proof. He cites the Quran where Allah reports the polytheists dismissing the Quran as 'only the speech of a human being.' Ashari then draws a logical implication: anyone who says the Quran is created is in fact agreeing with the polytheists, making the Quran human speech. Since Allah condemned that statement, the position that the Quran is created is invalid. Prepare to see how Ashari uses this simple yet powerful argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Ashari uses a very direct scriptural citation.
2
Identify the Quranic verse and its context
The verse is from Surah Al-Muddaththir (74:25). It reports what the polytheists said about the Quran. Understand that this is a statement Allah is condemning.
3
Understand Ashari's logical move
Ashari equates 'created' with 'human speech'. He argues that anyone who says the Quran is created is effectively saying it is human speech, because created things are not divine speech.
This is a key implication: creation implies being from humans, not from Allah.
4
Note the implication of divine condemnation
Since Allah condemned the polytheists for that statement, anyone who repeats it (by calling the Quran created) falls under the same condemnation. Therefore, the Quran cannot be created.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
5
Reflect on the argument's strength
Consider why this scriptural proof is compelling. It ties the theological position directly to a Quranic verse and shows that the createdness claim contradicts Allah's own words.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يبطل قولهم أن الله عز وجل قال مخبراً عن المشركين أنهم قالوا: ) إِنْ هَذَا إِلَّا قَولُ الْبَشَرِ ﴾ [المدثر : ۲۵] يعني القرآن فمن زعم أن القرآن مخلوق فقد جعله قولاً للبشر، وهذا ما أنكره الله على المشركين .
And among what invalidates their statement is that Allah Almighty said, informing about the polytheists that they said: 'This is not but the speech of a human being' [Al-Muddaththir:25] meaning the Quran. So whoever claims that the Quran is created has made it the speech of humans, and this is what Allah denied upon the polytheists.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is a scriptural proof by implication. Imam Ashari cites the Quran where Allah reports that the polytheists dismissed the Quran as mere human speech. He then argues that anyone who says the Quran is created is essentially agreeing with the polytheists and saying it is human speech. Since Allah condemned the polytheists for this statement, claiming the Quran is created is a false and blameworthy position. Therefore, the Quran is not created.

Key Terms
قول البشر (qawl al-bashar)
القرآن (al-Quran)
مخلوق (makhluq)
المشركين (al-mushrikeen)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'created' is different from 'human speech', so equating them is a false analogy.
Correction: Ashari's argument does not rely on a mere analogy; it uses the logical implication that if something is created, it is not divine and thus must be from a created source. The polytheists explicitly called the Quran 'human speech' and Allah condemned them. So claiming creation leads to the same condemnation.

Checkpoint

A) He says the disbelievers were correct
B) He says claiming the Quran is created is similar to claiming it is human speech, which Allah condemned
C) He says the disbelievers were ignorant
D) He says the Quran is both created and uncreated

Key Takeaway
Imam Ashari argues that claiming the Quran is created is equivalent to the polytheists' statement that it is human speech, which Allah condemned, so the Quran cannot be created.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

The Burning Bush Argument: Why God's Speech Cannot Be Created
Al-Ash'ari refutes creation of speech using the tree that spoke to Moses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's argument that God's speech cannot be created in a creature, using the example of the tree that spoke to Moses.

Core Idea
If God's speech were created in a tree, the tree would claim to be God—impossible.

In this passage, al-Ash'ari presents a powerful reductio ad absurdum against the Jahmiyya claim that God's speech is created. He uses the well-known story of the burning bush where a tree speaks to Moses. By examining what it would mean for God's speech to be 'in' that tree, he exposes a theological absurdity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its literal translation. Let the argument's flow become clear.
The Arabic may have an OCR issue at the start; the translation helps.
2
Identify the refuted claim
Notice that the passage argues against the idea that God's speech is created (makhluq) and can be placed in a creature.
3
Follow the logical steps
Trace the argument: if speech were created in the tree, then the tree would be the speaker of 'I am Allah'—an obvious absurdity since a tree cannot be divine.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Examine the Quranic support
Al-Ash'ari quotes Quran 32:13 to show that God's speech is 'from Him', not from a created thing.
This reinforces that speech is an attribute of God.
5
Connect to the conclusion
Understand that the passage concludes that God's speech cannot be created in another, just as His knowledge cannot be created in another.
This establishes speech as an eternal attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حل في شجرة، وكانت الشجرة حاوية له؛ فلزمهم أن تكون الشجرة بذلك الكلام متكلمةً، ووجب عليهم أن مخلوقاً من المخلوقين كلّم موسى صلى الله عليه وسلم، وأن الشجرة قالت: يا موسى إنَّني أنا الله لا إله إلا أنا فاعبدني، فلو كان كلام الله مخلوقاً في شجرة، لكان المخلوق قال : يا موسى إنَّني أنا الله لا إله إلا أنا فاعبدني، وقد قال الله عز وجل: وَلَكِن حَقَّ الْقَوْلُ مِن لَأَمْلَأَنَّ جَهَنَّمَ مِنَ الْجِنَّةِ وَالنَّاسِ أَجْمَعِينَ ﴾ [السجدة : ١٣] . وكلام الله من الله عز وجل لا يجوز أن يكون كلامه الذي هو منـه مخلوقاً في شجرة مخلوقة، كما لا يجوز أن يكون علمه الذي هو منه مخلوقاً في غيره، تعالى الله ذلك علواً كبيراً .
It was placed in a tree, and the tree contained it; thus it is necessary for them that the tree by that speech was speaking, and it is obligatory for them that a created being among creation spoke to Moses, peace be upon him, and that the tree said: 'O Moses, indeed I am Allah, there is no god but Me, so worship Me.' So if the speech of Allah were created in a tree, then the created thing would have said: 'O Moses, indeed I am Allah, there is no god but Me, so worship Me.' And Allah, Mighty and Majestic, said: 'But the word from Me was justified: I will surely fill Hell with jinn and people all together.' [Sajdah 32:13]. And the speech of Allah is from Allah, Mighty and Majestic; it is not permissible that His speech which is from Him be created in a created tree, just as it is not permissible that His knowledge which is from Him be created in another, exalted is Allah above that, a great exaltation.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage presents a proof by reductio ad absurdum against the Jahmiyya claim that God's speech is created in a creature. The author reasons: if God's speech were created in a tree (as in the story of Moses), then the tree would be the actual speaker of the divine words 'I am Allah' — an absurdity because a created tree cannot be the speaker of divinity. The author supports this with Quran 32:13, which affirms that God's word is from Him, not from a creature. The conclusion is that God's speech cannot be created in anything else, just as His knowledge cannot be created in another. Thus, speech is an eternal attribute of God, not a created accident in a substrate.

Key Terms
كلام الله
مخلوق
شجرة
متكلمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God creates speech in a tree, the tree only conveys it without actually speaking—the speech remains God's.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari insists that if the speech is created in the tree, the tree is the subject of the speech act, making it the speaker of 'I am Allah', which is impossible for a creature.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
God's speech cannot be created in a creature because that would make the creature the speaker of divine words, an impossibility; therefore, speech is an eternal attribute of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Impossibility of Creating God's Speech in a Creature
Al-Ash'ari draws an analogy between God's will and speech to refute creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Ash'ari argues that God's speech, like His will, cannot be created in a creature without attributing creaturehood to the divine attribute.

Core Idea
God's speech cannot be created in a creature because that would make the creature the actual speaker.

Al-Ash'ari continues his refutation of those who claim God's speech can be created in creatures. He draws a powerful analogy: just as it is impossible for God to place His will in a creature without that creature becoming the one who wills, it is likewise impossible for God to place His speech in a creature without that creature becoming the speaker. This brief but incisive argument preserves the transcendence of God's attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text slowly, noting the parallel structure between will and speech.
2
Identify the analogy
Notice how al-Ash'ari compares the impossibility of creating will with the impossibility of creating speech.
3
Understand the consequence
Grasp that if God's attribute were created in a creature, the creature would be the subject of that attribute, which is impossible.
4
Reflect on the implication
Think about why this argument safeguards God's unique attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال لهم : كما لا يجوز أن يخلق الله عز وجل إرادته في بعض المخلوقات، كذلك لا يجوز أن يخلق كلامه في بعض المخلوقات، ولو كانت إرادة الله مخلوقة في بعض المخلوقات، لكان ذلك المخلوق الله هو المريد بها، وذلك يستحيل . وكذلك يستحيل أن يخلق الله كلامه في مخلوق؛ لأن هذا يوجب أن ذلك المخلوق متكلم به ويستحيل أن يكون كلام الله عز وجل كلاماً للمخلوق .
And it is said to them: Just as it is not permissible that Allah, Mighty and Majestic, create His will in some created things, likewise it is not permissible that He create His speech in some created things. And if the will of Allah were created in some created things, then that created thing would be the one willing by it, and that is impossible. And likewise, it is impossible that Allah create His speech in a created thing, because this necessitates that that created thing is speaking with it, and it is impossible that the speech of Allah, Mighty and Majestic, be speech of a created thing.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is a response (jawaab) that uses an analogical argument. The author compares speech to will: just as it is impossible for God to create His will in a creature (because then the creature would be the one who wills, making it like God), it is also impossible for God to create His speech in a creature. If God's speech were created in a creature, that creature would be the speaker of those words, and the speech would belong to the creature, not to God. This is impossible because God's speech is an attribute of His essence, not a created accident in another being.

مريد
متكلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God's speech can be created in a creature as sounds are created in the air.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari argues that if speech were created in a creature, the creature would be the actual speaker, which is impossible for God's eternal attribute.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ash'ari, what would happen if God created His will in a created thing?
A) The created thing would become good.
B) The created thing would be the one willing by it.
C) The will would become independent.
D) God would lose His will.

Key Takeaway
God's speech, like His will, is an eternal attribute that cannot be created in a creature without violating His transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If God's attributes cannot be transferred to any creature, what does that mean for how you view the Qur'an as a physical object (paper and ink)? Is your heart attached to the divine attribute or the mere creation?
?
When you hear verses about Allah's will and speech, do you humbly accept that they are beyond your full comprehension, or do you secretly reduce them to human categories? What repentance might that require?

The Quran Is Not Human Speech: Proof from Surah 74:25
Al-Ash'ari uses Quran 74:25 to prove the Quran is not created.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari uses the Quranic condemnation of polytheists to prove that the Quran is uncreated.

Core Idea
If the Quran were created, it would be human speech—and Allah condemned that.

In this brief but powerful argument, al-Ash'ari turns the accusation of the polytheists into a proof. The polytheists dismissed the Quran as mere human speech; Allah recorded their statement and condemned it. Al-Ash'ari argues that anyone who claims the Quran is created is making the same claim, thereby falling under the same condemnation. This shows that the Quran must be uncreated divine speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English carefully. Note that al-Ash'ari quotes the verse directly.
The verse is Surah al-Muddaththir 74:25.
2
Identify the logical structure
The argument is: (1) The polytheists said the Quran is human speech. (2) Allah condemned that statement. (3) Saying the Quran is created is equivalent to saying it is human speech. (4) Therefore, saying it is created is condemned.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
3
Reflect on the implication
Understand why al-Ash'ari thinks 'created' equals 'human speech'. In his theology, only created beings produce created speech; divine speech must be uncreated.
This connects to the broader doctrine of the uncreated Quran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يبطل قولهم أن الله عز وجل قال مخبراً عن المشركين أنهم قالوا: إِنْ هَذَا إِلَّا قَولُ الْبَشَرِ ﴾ [المدثر : ۲۵] يعني القرآن فمن زعم أن القرآن مخلوق فقد جعله قولاً للبشر، وهذا ما أنكره الله على المشركين .
And among what invalidates their saying is that Allah, Mighty and Majestic, said informing about the polytheists that they said: 'This is nothing but the word of a human' [Muddaththir 74:25], meaning the Quran. So whoever claims that the Quran is created has made it the speech of humans, and this is what Allah denied upon the polytheists.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This is another proof (daleel aakhar) against the Jahmiyya. Al-Ash'ari cites Quran 74:25, where the polytheists accused the Quran of being mere human speech. He argues that by claiming the Quran is created, the Jahmiyya are effectively agreeing with the polytheists' accusation, which Allah condemned. Therefore, the Quran cannot be created; it is the uncreated speech of Allah.

Key Terms

مخلوق
قرآن
مشركين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that calling the Quran 'created' does not imply it is human speech, since Allah creates many things that are not human speech.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari argues that the Quran is speech (kalam), and if it is created, it must be the speech of a created being (human), because only created beings produce created speech. Divine speech is uncreated.

Checkpoint
What does al-Ash'ari say about those who claim the Quran is created?
A) They are correct because the Quran is in Arabic.
B) They are equating the Quran with human speech, which Allah denied.
C) They affirm the Quran is from Allah.
D) They are ignorant of grammar.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari proves the Quran's uncreatedness by showing that claiming it is created aligns with the polytheists' statement that Allah condemned.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The polytheists denied the Quran's divine origin and attributed it to human invention. How often do you, by neglecting its guidance, effectively treat the Quran as if it were merely human words? What would it take for you to submit to its authority as divine speech?
