Refutation of Created Speech via the Speaking Arm
Imam Ashari refutes the Mu'tazilite claim that God's speech is created in something else by analogy with the speaking arm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ashari uses the analogy of the speaking arm to refute the Mu'tazilite doctrine of created speech, exposing its logical inconsistency.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazilite view leads to the absurd conclusion that God said 'Do not eat me.'

This lesson presents one of Imam Ashari's sharpest refutations. He confronts the Mu'tazilites with a dilemma: if they claim God's speech is created in a tree, then by the same logic, the speech from the arm of a sheep (a hadith) would also be God's speech, leading to a blatantly absurd statement. The argument hinges on consistency.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazilite claim
The Mu'tazilites say that when Allah spoke to Musa, He created speech in the tree. Recognize that this is their starting position.
They hold that speech is an accident and cannot be an attribute of God.
2
Recognize the parallel case
Imam Ashari brings up the hadith where a foreleg of a sheep speaks to the Prophet, warning it is poisoned. The Mu'tazilites accept this as a miracle, but they must also consider the speech created in that arm.
3
See the dilemma
If they consider the arm's speech as created, then by their own logic it must be God's speech, making God say 'Do not eat me' – an absurdity. If they deny it's God's speech, then they contradict their own principle about the tree. Either way, their position fails.
This shows their doctrine is internally inconsistent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم : إذا زعمتم أن معنى أن الله عز وجل كلّم موسى أنه خلق كلاماً كلمه به في الشجرة، وقد خلق الله عندكم في الذراع كلاماً؛ لأن الذراع قالت: لا تَأْكُلْني فَإِنِّي مَسمُومَة . فلزمكم أن ذلك الكلام الذي سمعه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كلام الله عز وجل، فإن استحال أن يكون الله تكلم بذلك الكلام المخلوق فما أنكرتم من أنه مستحيل أن يخلق الله عز وجل كلامه في شجرة؛ لأن كلام المخلوق لا يكون كلاماً لله، فإن كان كلام الله، وكان معنى أن الله تكلم عندكم أنه خلق الكلام، فيلزمكم أن يكون الله متكلماً بالكلام الذي خلقه في الذراع. فإن أجابوا إلى ذلك قيل لهم : فالله عز وجل على قولكم هو القائل: لا تأكلني فإني مسمومة تعالى الله عن قولكم وافترائكم عليه علواً كبيراً . وإن قالوا: لا يجوز أن يكون كلام الله مخلوقاً في ذراع. قيل لهم : وكذلك لا يجوز أن يكون كلام الله مخلوقاً في شجرة .
Then it is said to them: If you claim that the meaning of Allah, Exalted and Majestic, speaking to Musa is that He created speech with which He spoke to him in the tree, and you hold that Allah created speech in the arm (of the sheep), because the arm said: 'Do not eat me, for I am poisoned.' Then it necessarily follows that that speech which the Prophet (peace be upon him) heard is the speech of Allah, Exalted and Majestic. If it is impossible that Allah spoke by that created speech, then why do you deny that it is impossible that Allah, Exalted and Majestic, creates His speech in a tree? Because the speech of a created being cannot be the speech of Allah. If it were the speech of Allah, and according to you the meaning of Allah speaking is that He created speech, then it necessarily follows that Allah is the speaker of the speech He created in the arm. If they answer affirmatively, it is said to them: Then Allah, Exalted and Majestic, according to your statement, is the one who says: 'Do not eat me, for I am poisoned'—exalted is Allah above your statement and your slander against Him, with great exaltation. And if they say: It is not permissible that the speech of Allah be created in an arm, it is said to them: Likewise, it is not permissible that the speech of Allah be created in a tree.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite doctrine that God's speech is created in something else. The author presents a dilemma to the opponents. They claim that God created speech in the tree for Musa. However, they also accept a hadith in which the foreleg of a sheep (الذراع) spoke to the Prophet, warning him not to eat it because it was poisoned. If the speech from the arm is created, then according to their own principle, it would be the speech of God, which is absurd because God would then be saying 'Do not eat me.' If they deny that the arm's speech is God's speech, then they contradict themselves regarding the tree. Thus, the argument exposes the inconsistency: if the arm's speech cannot be God's speech, neither can the tree's speech. The author concludes by affirming that God is far above such attributions.

Key Terms
كلام الله
كلام مخلوق
ذراع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the argument is simply that the arm's speech is impossible or that the miracle is being denied.
Correction: The point is the logical contradiction: the Mu'tazilites cannot consistently hold that speech in a tree is God's speech while denying that speech in an arm is God's speech, because the same principle applies.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Ashari, why does the Mu'tazilite position on God's speech lead to absurdity?
A) Because it requires God to be a created being
B) Because it forces them to accept that God spoke through the arm of a sheep, which is absurd
C) Because it denies the miracle of the tree
D) Because it contradicts the Quran

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite doctrine of created speech is self-refuting because it leads to an absurd consequence when applied consistently.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the Mu'tazilite attempt to protect God's transcendence by denying His speech an eternal attribute, can you see that same well-meaning but misguided reasoning in your own efforts to 'protect' Allah's majesty? In what area of your life are you prone to rationalize an interpretation that, on deeper scrutiny, leads to an absurd consequence about Allah? What will you do to correct it today?
?
The argument shows that a small inconsistency in doctrine can lead to attributing something unworthy to Allah. Where in your own beliefs about Allah—perhaps in your understanding of His attributes or actions—do you have a hidden inconsistency that you haven't confronted? What would it cost you to resolve it, and are you willing to pay that price?
?
The arm's speech, if taken as created, would make Allah say 'Do not eat me.' This is obviously false, yet the Mu'tazilites persisted. Is there any belief you hold about Allah that, if followed to its logical conclusion, would lead to something you know deep down is beneath His majesty? Will you examine it now and seek the truth regardless of the discomfort?
